Misconception: That invention and creation are distinct, so 'invention occurs through creation' is a meaningful statement.
Correction: The author shows that invention and creation are synonymous terms; thus the opponent's statement is self-contradictory.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what should the opponent have said about existence occurring through the attribute?
A) It proves the attribute is power
B) It proves the attribute is creation
C) It is impossible because existence comes from ijad
D) It is the same as invention

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the opponent's attempt to reduce khalq to power by clarifying that invention and creation are synonyms, and existence is from ijad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you ever confuse your own abilities (your 'power') with God's direct act of bringing things into existence (ijad)? How would acknowledging that all existence is from His ijad change the way you pray and rely on Him?
?
When you look at something you've achieved—like a skill or a relationship—do you attribute its existence to your effort or to God's creative act? What specific habit could you adopt to remind yourself that 'existence occurs through ijad, not power'?
?
The author insists that invention and creation are synonyms. Have you ever treated God's attributes as separate 'tools' rather than aspects of His single, all-encompassing act? How can you begin to see His creation as a direct, unified expression of His will?

The Flaw in the Opponent's Conclusion
Refutation of opponent's conclusion from divisional elimination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that even if only one division remains, it may still be impossible, so the opponent's conclusion is invalid.

Core Idea
A remaining possibility is not necessarily true; it may be impossible.

After attempting to refute the remaining division, the opponent concludes that since all divisions are invalid, khalq is not additional. The author strikes back: even if one division remains, it could be just as impossible as the others. He draws parallels to other sectarian positions to show inconsistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's conclusion
Identify the opponent's final claim: because all divisions are invalid, khalq is not additional to the created.
The opponent thinks he has eliminated all possibilities.
2
Understand the author's logical riposte
The author argues that the remaining division may itself be impossible; its mere survival doesn't make it possible.
This is a crucial logical point: elimination of others does not prove the remaining one.
3
Consider the examples
The author gives two examples: takwin as an attribute not in a place (Maturidi view) and Karramiyya's view. Both are rejected by the opponent, showing inconsistency.
The opponent cannot consistently accept the remaining division without accepting analogous views.

Proof that Takwin is an Eternal Attribute
Proof that takwin is eternal after establishing its distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument proving that takwin (making) is an eternal attribute of Allah, and why its origination is impossible.

Core Idea
Takwin must be eternal because any originated existence is logically impossible.

After establishing that takwin is distinct from the made, Imam al-Nasafi now turns to proving its eternity. He presents a logical dilemma: takwin must be either eternal or originated. If originated, it would have to fall into one of several categories, all of which have been proven impossible. Therefore, the only valid conclusion is that takwin is eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Get a sense of the overall argument.
Pay attention to the flow from premise to conclusion.
2
Identify the dilemma
The author presents two possibilities: takwin is either eternal or originated. Notice how he frames this as an exclusive disjunction.
3
Understand why originated is impossible
The passage argues that if takwin were originated, it would have to fall into three main divisions, each further divided into two, all of which are impossible. The author doesn't list them here, but emphasizes that their impossibility has already been proven.
The proof relies on a prior establishment of the impossibility of those categories.
4
Connect to the sects' doubts
The author references the objections of erring sects: that the claim is an innovation, and that eternal takwin implies eternal made. Notice how the argument refutes these by maintaining the distinction between attribute and its object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت التكوين غير المكون فبعد ذلك نصرف العناية إلى إثبات قدم التكوين، وقد خالفنا في ذلك جميع فرق الضلال على ما بينا في أول المسألة، وشبهتهم ما مر أنها مقالة محدثة على ما قررنا والثاني أن القول بقدم التكوين يوجب القول بقدم المكون فنقول: إذا ثبت أن التكون غير المكون لما ذكرنا من الدلائل فنقول بعد ذلك: إنه لا يخلو إما أن كان أزليا كما قلنا، وإما أن كان محدثا . ولا وجه لكونه محدثا لأنه ينقسم إلى أقسام ثلاثة ثم ينقسم كل قسم إلى قسمين وكلها ممتنعة، وفي القول بها ممتنعا إذ لا بد عند القول بحدوثه من إثباته على أحد هذه الأقسام الثلاثة ثم على أحد القسمين، فيكون ذلك إثبات ما قام دليل امتناعه وهو باطل.
Making (al-takwin) is an eternal, ancient attribute: And when it is established that making (al-takwin) is other than the made (al-mukawwan), then after that we direct attention to proving the eternity of making. And we have disagreed with all the sects of error in that, as we clarified at the beginning of the issue. And their doubt is that which passed: that it is an invented statement according to what we established. And the second is that the statement of the eternity of making necessitates the statement of the eternity of the made. So we say: When it is established that making is other than the made due to the proofs we mentioned, we then say: It must either be eternal (azali) as we say, or originated (muhdath). There is no aspect to its being originated, because it is divided into three divisions, then each division is divided into two, and all are impossible. And in saying it is impossible, since it is necessary when saying it is originated to establish it on one of these three divisions, then on one of the two subdivisions, and that would be establishing something whose impossibility has been proven, and it is false.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a proof that takwin (making) is an eternal attribute of God. The author first reminds that it has already been established that takwin is distinct from the made thing (mukawwan). Now he moves to prove its eternity. He notes that all erring sects oppose this, their first doubt being that the claim is an innovation, and their second being that if takwin is eternal, then the made thing (the world) would also be eternal. The author then presents a dilemma: takwin must be either eternal or originated. To prove its eternity, he argues that it cannot be originated because any originated thing must fall into certain classifications (presumably in terms of its subsistence and mode), and these classifications have all been proven impossible. Therefore, the only remaining possibility is that takwin is eternal. The logic is that if takwin were originated, it would have to be in one of several mutually exclusive categories, but each category has been shown to be impossible, so the premise of its origination is false, leading to the conclusion of its eternity.

Key Terms
التكوين
المكون
أزلي
محدث
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that if takwin is eternal, then the made must also be eternal.
Correction: The author emphasizes that takwin is distinct from the made; the eternity of the attribute does not entail the eternity of its object. The proof for eternity does not assume the eternity of the world.

Checkpoint
Why does the author conclude that takwin must be eternal?
A) Because it is the same as the divine essence
B) Because if it were originated, it would fall into impossible divisions
C) Because the opponent's arguments are weak
D) Because the Quran states it clearly

Key Takeaway
Takwin is eternal because its origination would require impossible categories, so only eternity remains.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If takwin is an eternal attribute of Allah, meaning His act of making never ceases, how does that change your awareness of His constant involvement in your life right now—your next breath, your next thought? What would it mean to live each moment with the certainty that Allah is actively making you, sustaining you?
?
The argument proves takwin's eternity by showing that any alternative is logically impossible. In your own faith, do you sometimes treat matters of intellect and reason as separate from matters of heart? How does this lesson challenge you to embrace both reason and certainty in your relationship with Allah?
?
The author says all sects of error oppose this truth. Have you ever felt alone in a belief you know is true because others around you disagree? This passage calls you to hold fast to truth even when it is unpopular. What is one belief about Allah that you hold firmly, and does your life reflect that conviction?

Proof of the Eternity of al-Takwin by Exhaustive Division
Nasafi proves the eternity of al-Takwin by exhaustive division and refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses an exhaustive division argument to prove that the attribute of al-Takwin is pre-eternal and not originated.

Core Idea
Al-Takwin must be eternal because every possible form of its origination leads to impossibility.

In this passage, Nasafi turns to proving the pre-eternity of al-Takwin after establishing that it is distinct from the things it brings into existence. He anticipates objections from deviant sects and systematically refutes all possible ways al-Takwin could be originated. By showing that each division and subdivision is impossible, he solidifies the doctrine that this divine attribute is eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the logical structure: first a claim, then a division into possibilities, then refutation of each.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the primary divisions
Nasafi divides the possibility of origination into three: in a locus other than Allah's essence, without a locus, or in Allah's essence. Identify these.
3
Follow the subdivisions
Each primary division is subdivided into two: occurring by itself or by Allah's causing. This creates six total options.
The refutation begins with the first subdivision.
4
See the infinite regress argument
The first option (occurrence in a locus other than Allah, caused by Allah) leads to an infinite regress of takwins, which is absurd because it would prevent the world from existing.
This is similar to Mu'ammar's doctrine.
5
Note the self-defeating nature
Nasafi points out that the infinite regress view actually implies the pre-eternity of the world, which would negate takwin—a self-refuting position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[التكوين صفة أزلية قديمة] وإذا ثبت التكوين غير المكون فبعد ذلك (۲) نصرف العناية إلى إثبات قدم التكوين، وقد خالفنا في ذلك جميع فرق الضلال على ما بينا في أول المسألة، وشبهتهم ما مر أنها مقالة محدثة على ما قررنا والثاني أن القول بقدم التكوين يوجب القول بقدم المكون فنقول: إذا ثبت أن التكون غير المكون لما ذكرنا من الدلائل فنقول بعد ذلك: إنه لا (۳) يخلو إما أن كان أزليا كما قلنا، وإما أن كان محدثا . ولا وجه لكونه محدثا لأنه ينقسم(4) إلى أقسام ثلاثة ثم ينقسم كل قسم إلى قسمين وكلها ممتنعة، وفي القول بها ممتنعا إذ لا بد عند القول بحدوثه من إثباته على أحد هذه الأقسام الثلاثة ثم على أحد القسمين، فيكون ذلك إثبات ما قام دليل امتناعه وهو باطل. [بيان الأقسام الثلاثة] وبيان تلك الأقسام الأولية : أنه إما أن حدث في محل سوى ذات الله تعالى، أو حدث لا في محل، أو حدث في ذات الله تعالى وكل قسم ينقسم إلى قسمين: إما أن حدث بنفسه أو بإحداث الله تعالى ولا وجه إلى القول بأن حدث بإحداث الله لأن الكلام في التكوين الثاني كهو في الأول، فيؤدي إلى إحداث التكوين الثاني بتكوين ثالث، والثالث برابع إلى ما لا يتناهى كما هو مذهب معمر (۳). وهو باطل، إذ القول بتعلق حدوث العالم بما لا يتناهى من الأسباب يمنع من حدوثه ووجوده، وهو موجود بالحس، محدث بالدليل الضروري فكان ذلك دليلا على بطلان هذه المقالة وهو مثل قول الدهرية لا حادث إلا وقبله حادث، وقد بينا فساد ذلك، ولي القول بصحة هذا قول بقدم العالم (٤) ، والقول بقدمه يوجد ، بطلان التكوين، فإذا هذا قول يوجب صحته بطلانه. ولا وجه إلى القول بحدوثه لا بإحداث أحد، لأنه لو جاز هذا في التكوين لجاز في كل العالم وقد مر إبطال ذلك في مسألة إثبات الصانع. وليس يستقيم قول الكرامية إنه محدث بالقدرة، إذ من مذهبهم أن التكوين
[Al-Takwin is an eternal attribute] And when it is established that al-takwin (bringing into existence) is other than the brought-into-existence (al-mukawwan), then after that we turn our attention to proving the pre-eternity (qidam) of al-takwin. And all the deviant sects have opposed us in that, as we explained at the beginning of the issue. Their doubt is what has passed: that [the doctrine of pre-eternity of attributes] is an innovated statement, as we have established, and secondly that the statement of the pre-eternity of al-takwin necessitates the statement of the pre-eternity of the brought-into-existence. So we say: When it is established that al-takwin is other than al-mukawwan due to the proofs we mentioned, we then say: It is not free from either being pre-eternal as we say, or being originated (muhdath). And there is no possibility for it being originated because it divides into three divisions, then each division divides into two, and all are impossible. And in saying that they are impossible, because when one says it is originated, it is necessary to posit it in one of these three divisions and then in one of the two subdivisions, so that would be positing what evidence of its impossibility has been established, and that is false. [Explanation of the three divisions] And the explanation of those primary divisions is: either it occurs in a locus other than the essence of Allah Most High, or it occurs without a locus, or it occurs in the essence of Allah Most High. And each division divides into two: either it occurs by itself or by Allah's causing. And there is no possibility to say that it occurs by Allah's causing because the discussion concerning the second takwin is like it in the first, so it leads to the causing of the second takwin by a third takwin, and the third by a fourth, ad infinitum, as is the school of Mu'ammar. And it is false, for the statement that the occurrence of the world is connected to an infinite chain of causes prevents its occurrence and existence, while it exists empirically and is proven originated by necessary evidence. So that is evidence for the falsity of this statement, and it is like the statement of the Dahriyya (materialists) that no event occurs except after a previous event, and we have shown the corruption of that. And I think that the statement affirming this is a statement of the pre-eternity of the world, and the statement of its pre-eternity necessitates the falsity of al-takwin. So this statement is such that its correctness necessitates its own falsity. And there is no possibility to say that it occurs without any causing, because if this were permissible for al-takwin, it would be permissible for the entire world, and the refutation of that has already passed in the issue of proving the Maker. And the statement of the Karamiyya that it is originated by power (qudra) is not sound, for it is part of their school that al-takwin...
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof for the pre-eternity (qidam) of the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). After establishing that takwin is distinct from the thing brought into existence (mukawwan), the author turns to proving that takwin itself is pre-eternal (azali), not originated. He begins by stating that all deviant sects oppose this, and he mentions their objections: that this doctrine is an innovation and that the pre-eternity of takwin would imply the pre-eternity of the thing brought into existence. He then proceeds with a logical division: takwin must be either pre-eternal or originated. Since there is no way it could be originated, he presents a tripartite division of what is originated: it occurs either in a locus other than Allah's essence, or without a locus, or in Allah's essence. Each of these is then subdivided: the occurrence is either by itself or by Allah's causing. He refutes each possibility systematically. The first subdivision (occurrence in a locus other than Allah's essence caused by Allah) leads to an infinite regress (tasalsul) like the doctrine of Mu'ammar, which is false because it prevents the occurrence of the world — but the world exists empirically. This regress is akin to the materialists' claim that every event has a prior event. Such a view actually implies the pre-eternity of the world, which would negate takwin itself — a self-defeating position. The second subdivision (occurrence without any causing) would, if allowed for takwin, be allowed for all things, which has already been refuted in the proof of the Creator. Finally, the Karamiyya claim that takwin is originated by power (qudra) is rejected, though the sentence is cut off. The overall structure is an exhaustive argument by division and refutation, showing that no form of origination is possible for takwin, thus proving its pre-eternity.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that proving the eternity of al-Takwin would imply that the world is also eternal.
Correction: Nasafi argues the opposite: if al-Takwin were originated, that would lead to an infinite regress which would imply the world's pre-eternity. Thus, the eternity of al-Takwin is necessary to avoid that implication.

Checkpoint
What is the primary method used to prove that al-Takwin is pre-eternal (qadim)?
A) Direct scriptural evidence.
B) An exhaustive division of possibilities for its origination, showing each is impossible.
C) An appeal to consensus.
D) A proof from the impossibility of infinite regress alone.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's exhaustive division argument shows that al-Takwin cannot be originated, so it must be pre-eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If al-Takwin is an eternal attribute of Allah, then every single thing that comes into existence in your life—from the air in your lungs to the opportunities you receive—is directly caused by this attribute. How does this truth expose the illusion of self-sufficiency you often carry? Name one area where you have acted as if you are the ultimate cause of your success, and commit to a specific change in your daily routine to acknowledge Allah's eternal bringing into existence.

The Logical Flaw in Claiming Power Alone Suffices
First of two falsifications: logical absurdity if power alone sufficed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first logical argument against the claim that the world is originated by God's power without a distinct act of creation.

Core Idea
If power alone sufficed, power itself would be creation, leading to contradictions.

This lesson introduces the refuted position and examines the first of two falsifications presented by Imam Nasafi. The argument shows that if the world occurred by mere power, then power would be indistinguishable from creation, leading to the absurdity that the world is contingent but not created, and ultimately restricting God's power to His own essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the refuted position
Begin by reading the opening statement that presents the view being criticized: that there is nothing created in God's essence by His power without origination and creation, and then He creates the world by a creation subsisting in His essence.
This sets up the target of the refutation.
2
Identify the first falsification
Find where the author says 'one of them is that if it were by power...' and trace the logical steps: power would be creation, bringing-into-existence would be pre-eternal, and the world would be merely contingent, not created.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Reflect on the terminology distinction
Notice how the author distinguishes between 'contingent' (hadith) and 'created' (muhdath). Their opponents call creation (takwin) contingent, not created, because it does not occur by origination; but the world they call created. This leads to the contradiction that creation is God's only object of power, confining His power to His essence.
This shows the internal inconsistency of the view.
4
Summarize the first flaw
Write a one-sentence summary of the first flaw in your own words, capturing how the logical chain leads to a self-refuting position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما محدث في ذات الباري تعالى بقدرته لا بإحداث وتكوين، ثم يحدث جميع العالم بتكوين الله تعالى القائم بذاته لأن هذا فاسد من وجوه أحدها أنه لو كان بالقدرة لكانت القدرة تكوينا، لأن التكوين ليس إلا ما يتكون به المكون وكذا الإيجاد ليس إلا يوجد به الحادث، فإذا كان هذا في الحقيقة قولا بقدم الإيجاد، لأن القدرة عندهم أزلية، ولأن حدوث الفعل لو جاز بمجرد القدرة من غير الإيجاد والتكوين لجاز ذلك في جميع العالم فيكون العالم حادثا غير محدث موجودا بالقدرة، فيبطل القول بوجود التكوين، فيبطل القول بحدوثه بالقدرة، فيكون هذا أيضا قولا يوجب صحة بطلانه، وما هذا سبيله من الأقاويل فهو باطل. ولأن عندهم حدوث التكوين بالقدرة وحدوث جميع العالم بالتكوين، فيسمون التكوين حادثا لا محدثا، لأنه ما حدث بالإحداث ليكون محدثا ويسمون العالم محدثا لأن حدوثه كان بالإحداث، ويقولون المحدث ما وقع عليه الإحداث، فأما حادث لم يقع عليه الإحداث فهو ليس بمحدث. وكذا يسمون كلام الله تعالى حادثا لا محدثا مخلوقا، فكان التكوين هو مقدور الله تعالى لا غير وهو حادث في ذاته، والعالم ليس بمقدور الله فلم تكن الله تعالى قدرة إلا على ما في ذاته فأما على وراء ذلك فلا قدرة له عليه. وهذا فاسد من وجوده لما فيه من إزالة قدرة الله تعالى عن العالم واقتصار قدرته على ما في ذاته والقول به مما يوجب مسارعة العقلاء أجمع إلى إكفارهم، ولأن القول به إنكار لقوله تعالى: {وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ} وعندهم لا يقدر على شيء إلا على ما حدث في ذاته، ولأن من أجزاء العالم ما هو مقدور غير الله تعالى وهو أفعال الحيوانات أجمع فلو لم تكن مقدورة له مع جواز كونها مقدورة لغيره للزمه العجز، إذ زوال القدرة عما هو في نفسه مقدور لن يكون إلا عن عجز، وقد بينا ذلك فيما تقدم، وصار كل ما دب و درج مما له فعل اختياري قادرا على ما قصرت عنه قدرة الله تعالى. وبطلان هذا لا يخفى. فإذا بطل هذان القسمان، وكل قسم من الأقسام الثلاثة ينقسم إلى أحد هذين القسمين بطلت الأقسام كلها.
There is nothing created in the essence of the Exalted Creator by His power without origination and creation, then He creates the entire world by the creation (takwin) of Allah the Exalted that subsists in His essence. Because this is false from several aspects: one of them is that if it were by power, then power would be creation, because creation is only that by which the created thing is created, and similarly bringing into existence is only that by which the contingent occurs. So if this is in reality a statement of the pre-eternity of bringing into existence, because power is eternal according to them, and because if the occurrence of an act were permissible by mere power without bringing into existence and creation, then that would be permissible for the entire world, so the world would be contingent not created, existing by power, so the statement of the existence of creation would be invalidated, and the statement of its occurrence by power would be invalidated, so this too is a statement that necessitates the validity of its own falsity, and what is like this among statements is false. And because according to them, the occurrence of creation is by power and the occurrence of the entire world is by creation, so they call creation 'contingent' not 'created', because it did not occur by origination to be created, and they call the world 'created' because its occurrence is by origination. And they say the created is what origination has fallen upon. As for a contingent that has not had origination fall upon it, it is not created. Likewise, they call the speech of Allah the Exalted 'contingent' not 'created' or 'creature'. So creation is the object of power of Allah the Exalted only, and it is contingent in His essence, and the world is not an object of power of Allah, so Allah the Exalted has no power except over what is in His essence; as for beyond that, He has no power over it. And this is false from its existence because it entails removing the power of Allah the Exalted from the world and restricting His power to what is in His essence, and the statement of it necessitates that all rational people hasten to declare them disbelievers. And because the statement of it is a denial of His statement, the Exalted: {And He is over all things competent} (Quran 30:50), while according to them He has no power over anything except over what occurs in His essence. And because among the parts of the world are things that are objects of power of other than Allah the Exalted, namely all the actions of animals. So if they were not objects of power for Him, with the possibility of them being objects of power for others, then incapability would necessarily follow for Him, because the removal of power from what is in itself an object of power can only be due to incapability. And we have explained this previously. And every creeping and walking thing that has voluntary action becomes powerful over what the power of Allah the Exalted fell short of. And the falsity of this is not hidden. So if these two divisions are false, and every division of the three divisions is subsumed under one of these two divisions, then all the divisions are false.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific theological position that claims the world is originated solely by God's power (qudra) without a distinct act of creation (takwin) or origination (ihdath). The argument proceeds in several steps. First, the author states the position to be refuted: that there is nothing created in God's essence by His power without origination and creation, and then He creates the entire world by a creation (takwin) subsisting in His essence. The author then points out multiple logical flaws. The first flaw (wajh) is that if the world's occurrence were by power alone, then power itself would be creation, because creation is precisely that by which a thing is created. This would lead to saying that bringing into existence (ijad) is pre-eternal (qadim), since power is eternal in their view. If an act could occur by mere power without a distinct act of bringing into existence, then anything could occur that way, making the world 'contingent' (hadith) but not 'created' (muhdath), which contradicts their own terminology. They call creation (takwin) 'contingent' not 'created' because it doesn't occur by origination, and call the world 'created' because its occurrence is by origination. This leads to an absurdity: creation is the object of God's power only, and it is contingent in His essence, while the world is not an object of God's power, so God has power only over what is in His essence, not over anything else. The author then argues that this position is false because it removes God's power from the world and restricts it to His essence, which would lead rational people to declare them disbelievers. It also contradicts the Quranic verse {And He is over all things competent}. Furthermore, it implies that actions of animals, which are part of the world, are not under God's power, but since they are possible objects of power for others, God would be incapable if He could not control them. This is clearly false. The passage ends by stating that since these two divisions (of the view) are false, and all other divisions fall under them, they are all false.

إحداث
حادث
محدث
إيجاد

Misconception & Correction

Correction: This passage shows that such a view leads to logical contradictions, including that power would be creation and God's power would be confined to His essence.

Checkpoint
What is the immediate consequence of claiming that the world occurs by God's power alone without a distinct act of creation, according to the first argument?
A) Power would be identical to creation.
B) The world would be eternal.
C) Takwin would be unnecessary.
D) God's essence would change.

Key Takeaway
The first falsification demonstrates that the view leads to the absurd conclusion that power itself is creation and God's power is restricted to His essence.

The Theological Flaw and Its Absurd Consequences
Second falsification: theological and practical absurdities resulting from the view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument against the view, which shows that it removes God's power from the world, contradicts the Quran, and implies that animals have power over their actions that God lacks.

Core Idea
Restricting God's power to His essence denies His omnipotence and leads to blasphemy.

This lesson continues the refutation by presenting the second falsification, which is theological and practical. It argues that the view under critique effectively denies God's power over the world, contradicts the Quranic verse 'He is over all things competent', and leads to the unacceptable consequence that animals have power over their own actions while God does not. The passage concludes that all such divisions are false.

Guided Path
1
Read the second falsification
Read from 'وهذا فاسد من وجوده' to the end. Notice that the author starts by stating that this position removes God's power from the world and restricts it to His essence, which would lead rational people to declare them disbelievers.
This is a strong theological condemnation.
2
Examine the Quranic contradiction
The author quotes Quran 30:50 'He is over all things competent' and notes that according to this view, God has power only over what occurs in His essence, contradicting the verse.
This is a scriptural refutation.
3
Analyze the argument from animal actions
The passage argues that animals perform voluntary actions which are objects of power for them. If God does not have power over these actions, then either God is incapable (since the actions are possible objects of power) or these creatures are more powerful than God—both absurd.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that since the two main divisions of the view are false, and all other divisions fall under them, the entire position is false.
This wraps up the refutation.

There is nothing created in the essence of the Exalted Creator by His power without origination and creation, then He creates the entire world by the creation (takwin) of Allah the Exalted that subsists in His essence. And because according to them, the occurrence of creation is by power and the occurrence of the entire world is by creation, so they call creation 'contingent' not 'created', because it did not occur by origination to be created, and they call the world 'created' because its occurrence is by origination. And they say the created is what origination has fallen upon. As for a contingent that has not had origination fall upon it, it is not created. Likewise, they call the speech of Allah the Exalted 'contingent' not 'created' or 'creature'. And because among the parts of the world are things that are objects of power of other than Allah the Exalted, namely all the actions of animals. So if they were not objects of power for Him, with the possibility of them being objects of power for others, then incapability would necessarily follow for Him, because the removal of power from what is in itself an object of power can only be due to incapability. And we have explained this previously. And every creeping and walking thing that has voluntary action becomes powerful over what the power of Allah the Exalted fell short of. And the falsity of this is not hidden. So if these two divisions are false, and every division of the three divisions is subsumed under one of these two divisions, then all the divisions are false.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific theological position that claims the world is originated solely by God's power (qudra) without a distinct act of creation (takwin) or origination (ihdath). The argument proceeds in several steps. First, the author states the position to be refuted: that there is nothing created in God's essence by His power without origination and creation, and then He creates the entire world by a creation (takwin) subsisting in His essence. The author then points out multiple logical flaws. The first flaw (wajh) is that if the world's occurrence were by power alone, then power itself would be creation, because creation is precisely that by which a thing is created. This would lead to saying that bringing into existence (ijad) is pre-eternal (qadim), since power is eternal in their view. If an act could occur by mere power without a distinct act of bringing into existence, then anything could occur that way, making the world 'contingent' (hadith) but not 'created' (muhdath), which contradicts their own terminology. They call creation (takwin) 'contingent' not 'created' because it doesn't occur by origination, and call the world 'created' because its occurrence is by origination. This leads to an absurdity: creation is the object of God's power only, and it is contingent in His essence, while the world is not an object of God's power, so God has power only over what is in His essence, not over anything else. The author then argues that this position is false because it removes God's power from the world and restricts it to His essence, which would lead rational people to declare them disbelievers. It also contradicts the Quranic verse {And He is over all things competent}. Furthermore, it implies that actions of animals, which are part of the world, are not under God's power, but since they are possible objects of power for others, God would be incapable if He could not control them. This is clearly false. The passage ends by stating that since these two divisions (of the view) are false, and all other divisions fall under them, they are all false.

Key Terms
قدرة
تكوين
حادث
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that restricting God's power to His essence is a defensible theological position.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that this leads to takfir, contradicts the Quran, and implies absurdities like animals being more powerful than God.

Checkpoint
According to the second falsification, what does the view imply about the power of animals compared to God?
A) Animals have no power.
B) Animals have the same power as God.
C) Animals would have power over actions that God does not have.
D) Animals' actions are not objects of power.

Key Takeaway
The second falsification shows that the view removes God's power from the world, contradicts the Quran, and leads to the absurdity that animals have power God lacks.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God's power is limited, how would that affect your reliance on Him in moments of desperation? Can you identify an area in your life where you subconsciously act as if God's power is restricted?
?
The passage says rational people would hasten to declare such a view as disbelief. Have you ever entertained a thought about God that, upon closer examination, actually diminishes His majesty? What will you do to guard your heart against such thoughts?
?
The absurdity of animals having power God lacks is obvious—yet do you sometimes attribute outcomes to 'luck' or 'nature' as if they act independently of God's power? How can you train your mind to see Allah's power in every event?

The First Proof: Takwin as Accident Cannot Exist Without a Locus
First proof against takwin not in a locus, with objection and response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that takwin, being an accident, cannot subsist by itself, and how he refutes Ibn al-Rawandi's objection.

Core Idea
Accidents cannot exist alone—their very nature demands a subject.

Nasafi begins his refutation by addressing the first possibility: that takwin occurs not in a locus. He argues that takwin is an accident, and like all accidents, it cannot exist independently. He then tackles a counterargument from Ibn al-Rawandi, who redefines 'accident' to avoid this conclusion. Let's see how Nasafi turns this objection back on itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the first proof passage
Read the Arabic passage containing the first proof, its objection, and response. Notice the structure: statement, objection, counter-response.
Pay attention to how Nasafi uses the example of blackness and whiteness.
2
Identify the core claim and objection
Nasafi claims takwin is an accident and cannot exist without a locus. Ibn al-Rawandi objects by redefining accident as that which inheres in a substance, arguing takwin does not inhere.
Ibn al-Rawandi's definition seems plausible but leads to a contradiction.
3
Follow Nasafi's response
Nasafi points out that if the definition is changed, then other accidents like blackness could also be said to exist without a locus. This leads to absurdity. He then explains that the impossibility of self-subsistence is not due to the definition but to the intrinsic nature of accidents.
This is a deeper philosophical point about the nature of attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : كل قسم من ذلك باطل في نفسه أيضا. أما حدوثه لا في محل ففاسد من وجهين أحدهما أن التكوين الحادث عرض ووجود العرض قائما بنفسه محال كما في سائر الأعراض، كالسواد والبياض والحركة والسكون وغير ذلك من الأعراض ولن يستقيم قول صاحب هذه المقالة وهو ابن الراوندي أن التكوين ليس بعرض لأن العرض ما يعرض الجوهر فيوجد فيه، وهذا لا يعرض الجوهر بل يوجد لا في محل، والعرض هو الذي يستحيل قيامه بنفسه لا ما ليس عرضا. لأنا نقول له: جواز قيام السواد والبياض والحركة والسكون وغير ذلك لا في محل ، ولا تسميها أعراضا لأنها لم تعرض الجوهر؟ فإن جوز ذلك خرج عن المعقول والتحق بأهل العناد وإن لم يجوز بطل سعيه. ثم نقول : إن استحالة قيام هذه الأعراض بأنفسها ما كانت لأنها أعراض تعرض الجوهر، بل اعتراضها الجوهر ووجودها فيه لا غير، كان لاستحالة قيامها بذواتها فكانت مفتقرة إلى محل في أنفسها لما أنها صفات تتجلى بها محالها، وتمتاز بقيامها بها عما لا قيام لها بها، فلا يتصور وجودها لا على هذا السبيل. والوجه الثاني أن التكوين لو كان قائما لا في محل لم يكن الله تعالى به اختصاص فلم يكن هو به مكونا كما لا يكون الذات في المشاهد أسود بسواد لم يقم به فلم يكن الله تعالى خالق العالم فلم يكن العالم دالا عليه، والقول بهذا تعطيله ونفيه، ولو جاز أن يوصف الله تعالى به وإن لم يقم التكوين به، لجاز أن يوصف به غير الله تعالى وإن لم يكن للتكوين اختصاص به، فيكون لو حدث اليوم جسم لكان كل واحد من الناس مكونا له خالقا موجدا محدثا ، ولا يكون الله تعالى بكونه خالقا له أولى من كل من الناس، وفساد هذا لا يخفى، ولو وجد سواد لا في محل لكان كل الأجسام أسود به والقول بهذا كله خروج عن قضايا العقول فبطل هذا القسم.
Then we say: Every division of that is invalid in itself as well. As for its occurrence not in a locus, it is corrupt from two aspects: The first is that originated takwin is an accident, and the existence of an accident subsisting by itself is impossible just as in the case of other accidents, such as blackness, whiteness, motion, rest, and other accidents. And the statement of the proponent of this article—he being Ibn al-Rawandi—that takwin is not an accident because an accident is that which inheres in a substance and exists in it, while this (takwin) does not inhere in a substance but exists not in a locus, and the accident is that which is impossible to subsist by itself, not what is not an accident, will not stand. For we say to him: Is it permissible for blackness, whiteness, motion, rest, and others to exist not in a locus, and you do not call them accidents because they did not inhere in a substance? If he permits that, he departs from reason and joins the people of obstinacy; and if he does not permit it, his effort is nullified. Then we say: The impossibility of these accidents subsisting by themselves was not because they are accidents that inhere in a substance—rather their inherence in a substance and their existence in it is nothing else—but it was due to the impossibility of their subsisting by themselves. Thus they are in need of a locus in themselves, because they are attributes by which their loci are manifested and are distinguished by their subsistence in them from that which does not have subsistence in them. So their existence not in this manner is inconceivable. The second aspect: If takwin subsisted not in a locus, then God Most High would not be distinguished by it, so He would not be the maker (mukawwin) by it, just as a perceived essence is not black by a blackness that does not subsist in it. Then God Most High would not be the creator of the world, so the world would not indicate Him. And holding this is to negate Him and deny Him. And if it were permissible that God Most High be described by it even though takwin does not subsist in Him, then it would be permissible that other than God be described by it, even though takwin has no specification with him. So if a body came into existence today, every single person would be its maker, creator, bringer into existence, and originator, and God Most High would not be more entitled to be its creator than any of the people. The corruption of this is not hidden. And if blackness were found not in a locus, then all bodies would be black by it. Holding all this is a departure from the dictates of intellects. Thus this division is nullified.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the position that takwin (bringing into existence) can occur not in a locus, i.e., as a self-subsisting entity without inhering in a subject. The author presents two proofs. The first proof argues that takwin, being an accident, cannot exist by itself. He addresses an objection from Ibn al-Rawandi who claims takwin is not an accident because accident is defined as that which inheres in a substance, whereas takwin does not inhere. The author replies by turning the definition back on him: if the objector denies that takwin is an accident because it does not inhere, then by the same logic he must allow that other acknowledged accidents like blackness could also exist without inhering, which is absurd. The author then reinforces that accidents are intrinsically dependent on a locus; their impossibility of self-subsistence is not due to the definition of inherence but due to their very nature as attributes that need a subject. The second proof shows the theological absurdity: if takwin existed not in a locus, God would not be uniquely characterized by it, so He would not be the exclusive creator. This would lead to the conclusion that any person could be a creator, and that God would not be indicated by the world, resulting in atheism. The proof concludes that this division is invalid.

عرض
محل
اختصاص
ابن الراوندي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that redefining 'accident' as 'that which inheres in a substance' allows takwin to be considered a different category that can exist without a locus.
Correction: Nasafi shows that this redefinition leads to contradictions: if accepted, other accidents like blackness could also exist without a locus, which is absurd. Moreover, the need for a locus is not due to the definition but to the intrinsic nature of accidents as attributes that manifest subjects.

Checkpoint
What is the primary argument in the first proof against the possibility of takwin existing not in a locus?
A) Takwin is eternal
B) Takwin is an accident and cannot subsist by itself
C) Takwin requires a locus because it is a substance
D) Ibn al-Rawandi's definition is correct

Key Takeaway
The first proof establishes that takwin, being an accident, cannot exist without a locus, and redefining 'accident' does not escape this ontological fact.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that accidents cannot exist without a subject. But do you live as if God's attributes—His power, His knowledge—are real and essential to Him, or do you sometimes imagine them as detached concepts? Confront your own tendency to think of God's attributes as abstract ideas rather than as realities that define His very being.
?
Ibn al-Rawandi redefined 'accident' to escape the truth. When you encounter a truth about God that challenges your comfort, do you quietly redefine it in your mind to avoid submission? Ask yourself: where in your faith have you subtly shifted definitions to avoid accountability?
?
Nasafi calls departing from reason in this matter 'joining the people of obstinacy.' Are there areas in your beliefs where you cling to irrational positions because the truth demands change? Write down one belief you hold that you are afraid to test against the necessary truths of revelation.

The Second Proof: Theological Absurdity of Takwin Without a Locus
Second proof: theological absurdity of takwin not in a locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's second proof, which shows that if takwin existed not in a locus, it would lead to theological absurdities such as denying God's exclusive creativity and the world's ability to indicate Him.

Core Idea
If takwin were self-subsisting, God would not be the unique creator.

Nasafi now turns to a theological argument. He shows that if takwin (the act of bringing into existence) existed not in a locus, it would not be exclusively attributed to Allah. This would undermine the proof of God from creation and lead to the absurd conclusion that anyone could be a creator. Let's examine this second proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof passage
Read the Arabic text of the second proof. Notice how it builds a chain of logical consequences.
The proof is concise but dense with implications.
2
Identify the first consequence
Nasafi argues that if takwin were not in a locus, Allah would not be distinguished by it, so He would not be the maker (mukawwin) by it. This is like a body not being black by a blackness that doesn't inhere in it.
This parallels the analogy of accidents and subjects.
3
Follow the chain to denial of God
If Allah is not the maker by this takwin, then He would not be the creator of the world. Consequently, the world would not indicate Him, leading to atheism (ta'til).
Nasafi calls this 'negation and denial' of God.
4
Consider the reductio ad absurdum
Nasafi adds that if it were permissible for God to be described by a self-subsisting takwin, then anyone could be described by it, making every person a creator of anything that comes into existence. This is obviously false.
This shows the doctrine leads to multiple creators and undermines tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : كل قسم من ذلك باطل في نفسه أيضا. أما حدوثه لا في محل ففاسد من وجهين أحدهما أن التكوين الحادث عرض ووجود العرض قائما بنفسه محال كما في سائر الأعراض، كالسواد والبياض والحركة والسكون وغير ذلك من الأعراض ولن يستقيم قول صاحب هذه المقالة وهو ابن الراوندي أن التكوين ليس بعرض لأن العرض ما يعرض الجوهر فيوجد فيه، وهذا لا يعرض الجوهر بل يوجد لا في محل، والعرض هو الذي يستحيل قيامه بنفسه لا ما ليس عرضا. لأنا نقول له: جواز قيام السواد والبياض والحركة والسكون وغير ذلك لا في محل ، ولا تسميها أعراضا لأنها لم تعرض الجوهر؟ فإن جوز ذلك خرج عن المعقول والتحق بأهل العناد وإن لم يجوز بطل سعيه. ثم نقول : إن استحالة قيام هذه الأعراض بأنفسها ما كانت لأنها أعراض تعرض الجوهر، بل اعتراضها الجوهر ووجودها فيه لا غير، كان لاستحالة قيامها بذواتها فكانت مفتقرة إلى محل في أنفسها لما أنها صفات تتجلى بها محالها، وتمتاز بقيامها بها عما لا قيام لها بها، فلا يتصور وجودها لا على هذا السبيل. والوجه الثاني أن التكوين لو كان قائما لا في محل لم يكن الله تعالى به اختصاص فلم يكن هو به مكونا كما لا يكون الذات في المشاهد أسود بسواد لم يقم به فلم يكن الله تعالى خالق العالم فلم يكن العالم دالا عليه، والقول بهذا تعطيله ونفيه، ولو جاز أن يوصف الله تعالى به وإن لم يقم التكوين به، لجاز أن يوصف به غير الله تعالى وإن لم يكن للتكوين اختصاص به، فيكون لو حدث اليوم جسم لكان كل واحد من الناس مكونا له خالقا موجدا محدثا ، ولا يكون الله تعالى بكونه خالقا له أولى من كل من الناس، وفساد هذا لا يخفى، ولو وجد سواد لا في محل لكان كل الأجسام أسود به والقول بهذا كله خروج عن قضايا العقول فبطل هذا القسم.

Three Arguments Against Takwin in a Separate Locus
Nasafi enumerates three proofs against takwin subsisting in a locus other than God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational proofs that Nasafi uses to refute the possibility of the attribute of takwin (divine bringing into existence) subsisting in any locus other than the essence of God.

Core Idea
Takwin cannot require a separate carrier; that would compromise divine uniqueness and perfection.

In this passage, Nasafi presents three logical arguments against the idea that takwin—the divine act of bringing into existence—could inhere in a created entity or an eternal being other than God. Each proof targets a different fatal flaw: infinite regress, misattribution of creation, and the impossibility of a deficient eternal being.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three proofs
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting that Nasafi lists three proofs (wujuh) against takwin subsisting in a locus other than God. Each is introduced by a number (one, two, three).
The first proof references a prior argument; the second deals with attribution of creation; the third is a dilemma about the nature of the locus.
2
Analyze the first proof (infinite regress)
Understand that the first proof argues that if takwin requires another takwin, an infinite regress results. If it does not, then takwin cannot occur in a locus. Grasp the underlying reasoning.
This proof is brief and relies on an earlier detailed argument.
3
Examine the second proof (undermining divine agency)
Notice that if takwin subsists in a locus, then the one in whom it subsists would be the creator, not God. This contradicts the principle that God's attributes subsist in Him alone.
4
Study the third proof (dilemma of the locus)
Follow the dilemma: the locus is either eternal or originated. If eternal, it must possess attributes of perfection or not. If it lacks perfection, it cannot be eternal. If it possesses perfection and has takwin, it would be the creator. Therefore, only God can be the locus of takwin.
This proof demonstrates the absurdity of positing an eternal being other than God with creative power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حدوثه في محل آخر سوى ذات القديم فمحال فاسد أيضا لوجوه: أحدها بما مر من أن التكوين حدث بتكوين أم لا بتكوين إلى آخر ما بينا. والثاني أن التكوين لو كان قائما بمحل لكان المكون للعالم من قام به التكوين لا الله تعالى الصفات التي مر ذكرها أن الموصوف محالها لا غيرها، وقد قررنا كما في جميع ذلك غير مرة. والثالث أن ذلك المحل الذي قام به التكوين إما أن يكون قديما، وإما أن يكون محدثا ، فإن كان قديما إما أن كان موصوفا بصفات الكمال وإما أن لم يكن موصوفا بها، فإن لم يكن موصوفا بها فلا يكون قديما، إذ التعري عن صفات الكمال يوجب الاتصاف بأضدادها وهي كلها نقائص وذلك من أمارات الحدوث، ولو كان موصوفا بصفات الكمال والتكوين قائم به فهو الخالق للعالم المكون له لا ذلك الغير. وجاء من هذا ما ذهبنا إليه وأبيتم أنتم من إثبات صانع قديم للعالم كان التكوين صفة له قائمة به وبطل جميع سعيكم.
As for its occurrence in a locus other than the essence of the Eternal, it is impossible and corrupt as well, due to aspects: The first is what has already been mentioned: that takwin either occurs by another takwin or not, and so on to the end of what we explained. The second: if takwin subsisted in a locus, then the maker of the world would be the one in whom takwin subsists, not God Most High—[contrary to] the attributes which were previously mentioned, that the described (al-mawsuf) is their locus (mahalluha) and nothing else. And we have established that repeatedly. The third: that locus in which takwin subsists is either eternal or originated. If it is eternal, it either is described with attributes of perfection or not. If it is not described with them, then it cannot be eternal, because being devoid of attributes of perfection necessitates being described with their opposites, which are all deficiencies, and that is a sign of origination. And if it is described with attributes of perfection and takwin subsists in it, then it is the creator of the world, its maker, not that other [supposed eternal being]. And from this follows what we have held and you have refused to affirm: an eternal maker of the world for whom takwin is an attribute subsisting in Him, and all your effort is nullified.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage refutes the position that takwin could subsist in a locus other than God's essence. The author gives three proofs. The first proof references an earlier argument about whether takwin requires another takwin, leading to an infinite regress. The second proof points out that if takwin inheres in a locus, then the creative act is attributed to that locus, not to God; but the divine attributes are such that God is the locus of His attributes. The third proof is a detailed dilemma: the locus of takwin is either eternal or originated. If eternal, it either possesses perfect attributes or not. If it lacks perfection, it cannot be eternal, because deficiency indicates originatedness. If it possesses perfection and takwin subsists in it, then that locus itself would be the creator, not any other being. Thus, the only consistent position is the one the author holds: that there is an eternal maker, God, whose attribute of takwin subsists in Him. The opponents' efforts are therefore nullified.

Key Terms
تكوين
محل
قديم
محدث
صفات الكمال
خالق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Takwin could be an accident inhering in a created entity or an eternal being other than God.
Correction: Nasafi argues that if takwin inheres in a locus other than God, that locus would become the creator, implying either an infinite regress, a contradiction with divine agency, or the absurdity of an eternal being lacking perfection.

Checkpoint
In the third proof against takwin subsisting in a locus other than God, what conclusion does the author draw if the locus is eternal and possesses attributes of perfection?
A) The locus is an angel
B) The locus is a separate creator independent of God
C) The locus itself would be the Creator
D) The locus is a created thing

Key Takeaway
Takwin must be an attribute subsisting in God's essence; any other locus leads to absurd consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that nothing in the universe shares even the slightest measure of the power to create—that every effect is directly from Allah alone? Examine your heart: is there any being, concept, or cause to which you attribute independent influence?
?
When you witness the order and beauty of creation, do you ever feel a tug to think that nature itself has a kind of creative power? This lesson demands that you reject that—that only the One whose attribute of takwin is identical to His essence brings things into being. Will you consciously train your mind to see every effect as a direct act of Allah?
?
If takwin were separable from God, the universe would be without a true sustainer for an instant. This argument shows the logical necessity of God’s attributes being inseparable. How does this affect the way you rely on Allah for your daily existence? Do you truly depend on Him for each breath, or do you fall into heedlessness, thinking things happen on their own?

Takwin Cannot Be Self-Subsistent
Nasafi refutes the self-subsistence of takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why takwin (the divine attribute of creating) cannot be self-subsistent and must inhere in God's essence.

Core Idea
If takwin were self-subsistent, anyone could be a creator, leading to absurdity.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi presents the second argument against the view that the attribute of creating (takwin) exists independently of God. He shows that such a claim leads to logical contradictions, including the denial of God's unique role as Creator. Let's examine how he dismantles this position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim
The claim is that takwin subsists without a locus, i.e., it exists on its own, not inhering in God. This is the position being refuted.
2
First consequence: No special distinction
If takwin is self-subsistent, then God would have no special distinction by it, just as a thing is not black by a blackness that does not inhere in it. Thus God would not be the Creator, and the world would not indicate Him.
This leads to atheism (ta'til).
3
Second consequence: Anyone could be creator
If God could be described by a self-subsistent takwin, then anyone else could be described by it too, without special relation. So if a body came into existence, every person would be its creator.
This is obviously false.
4
Final absurdity: Blackness analogy
The argument is reinforced by analogy: if blackness existed without a locus, then every body would be black. Similarly, a self-subsistent takwin would make anything a creator.
All this contradicts reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثاني أن التكوين لو كان قائما لا في محل لم يكن الله تعالى به اختصاص فلم يكن هو به مكونا كما لا يكون الذات في المشاهد أسود بسواد لم يقم به فلم يكن الله تعالى خالق العالم فلم يكن العالم دالا عليه، والقول بهذا تعطيله ونفيه، ولو جاز أن يوصف الله تعالى به وإن لم يقم التكوين به، لجاز أن يوصف به غير الله تعالى وإن لم يكن للتكوين اختصاص به، فيكون لو حدث اليوم جسم لكان كل واحد من الناس مكونا له خالقا موجدا محدثا، ولا يكون الله تعالى بكونه خالقا له أولى من كل من الناس، وفساد هذا لا يخفى، ولو وجد سواد لا في محل لكان كل الأجسام أسود به والقول بهذا كله خروج عن قضايا العقول فبطل هذا القسم.
And the second aspect: that if takwin were subsisting not in a locus, then Allah (God) would have no special distinction by it, so He would not be a maker (mukawwin) by it, just as an essence in the observable world is not black by a blackness that does not subsist in it. Then Allah would not be the creator (khalq) of the world, and the world would not indicate Him. To say this is to negate and deny Him. And if it were permissible to describe Allah by it even though takwin does not subsist in Him, then it would be permissible to describe other than Allah by it even though takwin has no special relation to him. Thus if a body were to come into existence today, every person would be its maker, creator, originator, and bringer-into-existence, and Allah would have no more right to be its creator than any person. The corruption of this is not hidden. And if blackness existed not in a locus, then every body would be black by it. All this is departure from the dictates of intellects. So this division is false.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a proof against the claim that the attribute of creating (takwin) subsists without a locus (i.e., is self-subsistent). The author begins by stating the second of two aspects (the first was presumably about takwin subsisting in a locus, which is already refuted). He argues that if takwin were self-subsistent, then God would not be specifically characterized by it, just as a thing is not black by a blackness that does not inhere in it. Consequently, God would not be the creator of the world, and the world would not indicate Him—this amounts to atheism (ta'til). Furthermore, if it were allowed for God to be described by a self-subsistent takwin, then any other being could also be described by it without any special relation, leading to the absurdity that every person would be the creator of any new body. Finally, a self-subsistent blackness would make everything black—a manifest absurdity. Thus, the view is rejected as contrary to reason.

Key Terms
تكوين (takwin)
قائم لا في محل (self-subsistent)
اختصاص (special distinction)
تعطيل (negation of God)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Takwin is an attribute that does not need to inhere in God; it is self-subsistent.
Correction: The passage shows that if takwin were self-subsistent, God would not be uniquely the Creator, and anyone could claim to create, leading to polytheism and absurdity. Takwin must inhere in God's essence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if takwin were self-subsistent, what would happen if a new body came into existence?
A) Only God would create it.
B) Every person would be its creator.
C) Nobody would be its creator.
D) The body would create itself.

Key Takeaway
Takwin must inhere in God's essence; otherwise, divine uniqueness is undermined and absurd consequences follow.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If takwin must inhere in Allah alone for Him to be uniquely the Creator, then what is your role in your own accomplishments? Have you ever felt a sense of self-sufficiency, as if you created your own success? How does this lesson dismantle that illusion? Commit to repeating 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' whenever you feel pride in your own doing.
?
The analogy of blackness: if blackness were self-subsistent, every body would be black. Reflect on a time you attributed a quality or outcome to a secondary cause as if it were independent of Allah. What was that, and how will you now redirect that attribution solely to Allah? Write down one specific instance and repent.
?
Nasafi warns that denying the inherence of takwin leads to atheism (ta'til). Are there any subtle assumptions in your life that Allah is not directly involved in every detail? For example, do you ever think of natural processes as independent agents? Meditate on the verse 'Allah is the Creator of all things' and resolve to see His hand in every event today.

First Two Reasons Against Takwin in Another Locus
Imam Nasafi gives two preliminary arguments against takwin subsisting in another locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first two arguments Imam Nasafi uses to refute the possibility of the attribute of creating (takwin) subsisting in a locus other than God.

Core Idea
Takwin cannot reside in another locus; that would imply infinite regress or misattribute creation.

Imam Nasafi begins his refutation by presenting two preliminary arguments. The first recalls a previously established point about infinite regress, while the second asserts that an attribute's locus is the subject itself. These set the stage for a more detailed analysis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation.
Notice the structure: the author states the claim, then gives two reasons labeled 'one of them' and 'second'.
2
Identify the two reasons
Find reason 1 (the regress argument) and reason 2 (the locus argument). Understand what each is saying.
Reason 1 refers to an earlier argument about regress. Reason 2 is a logical principle: the attribute inheres in its subject.
3
Understand the significance
Ask yourself: why do these two reasons together form a strong opening? They eliminate the simplest alternatives.
These reasons set up the more complex third reason that follows.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حدوثه في محل آخر سوى ذات القديم فمحال فاسد أيضا لوجوه: أحدها بما مر من أن التكوين حدث بتكوين أم لا بتكوين إلى آخر ما بينا. والثاني أن التكوين لو كان قائما بمحل لكان المكون للعالم من قام به التكوين لا الله تعالى وقد قررنا الصفات التي مر ذكرها أن الموصوف محالها لا غيرها كما في جميع ذلك غير مرة. والثالث أن ذلك المحل الذي قام به التكوين إما أن يكون قديما وإما أن يكون محدثا، فإن كان قديما إما أن كان موصوفا بصفات الكمال وإما أن لم يكن موصوفا بها، فإن لم يكن موصوفا بها فلا يكون قديما، إذ التعري عن صفات الكمال يوجب الاتصاف بأضدادها وهي كلها نقائص وذلك من أمارات الحدوث، ولو كان موصوفا بصفات الكمال والتكوين قائم به فهو الخالق للعالم المكون له لا ذلك الغير. وجاء من هذا ما ذهبنا إليه وأبيتم أنتم من إثبات صانع قديم للعالم كان التكوين صفة له قائمة به وبطل جميع سعيكم. فبعد ذلك القول بإثبات قديم آخر لا تكون له باطل، إذ القول بالقديمين القائمين بالذات محال على ما مر. وكذلك جعل من له صفات الكمال وهو موصوف بالتكوين غير صانع للعالم، وجعل من لا تكون له صانعا له قلب المعقول فيكون باطلا. وإن كان ذلك المحل حادثا إما أن حدث بتكوين وإما أن حدث لا بتكوين. فإن حدث لا بتكوين، فإما أن حدث لا بمعنى من قبل الباري وإما أن حدث بالقدرة، ولا وجه إلى القول بحدوثه لا بمعنى من قبل الباري لأنه لو جاز ذلك فيه لجاز في جميع العالم وفيه تعطيل الصانع، ولا وجه للقول بحدوثه بالقدرة لا بتكوين لما مر أنه لو جاز هذا فيه لجاز في جميع العالم فبطل التكوين أصلا، فيكون العالم مقدور الله تعالى لا مخلوقه، ويكون الله قادرا على العالم لا خالقا له، والقول به كفر لما أن القدرة لا تقتضى الوجود بدون الفعل، فيكون فيه أيضا تعطيل الصانع. ولأن وجوده لو كان بالقدرة لكانت القدرة إيجادا وهي فكان الإيجاد أزنيا. ولو حدث بتكوين إما أن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه كما هو المحكي عن بشر بن المعتمر، وإما أن حدث بتكوين مقارن له كما هو المحكي عن أبي الهذيل، فإن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه فإذا لا قيام للتكوين به قبل وجوده إذ قيام تكوين موجود بمكون لم يوجد بعد محال، وقد أبطلنا قيام التكوين بنفسه، ولأنه لما جاز وجود التكوين ولا مكون بعد زمانا واحدا جاز أزمنة كثيرة إذ لا فرق بين التقدم بزمان والتقدم بأزمنة في أن وجوده ولا مكون جائز. وإذا كان كذلك بطل ادعاؤهم أن وجود التكوين يقتضي وجود المكون لا محالة ولا يجوز سبقه عليه ونبين هذا بأتم من ذلك في مسألة الاستطاعة إن شاء الله تعالى.
As for its occurrence in another locus besides the Eternal Essence, it is also impossible and corrupt, for reasons: One of them is what has already passed—that takwin occurred either by a takwin or not by a takwin, etc., up to what we explained. Second, that if takwin were subsisting in a locus, then the maker of the world would be the one in whom takwin subsists, not Allah; and we have established the attributes mentioned earlier, that the described thing's locus is its own, not another's, as we have repeatedly shown. Third, that locus in which takwin subsists is either eternal or originated. If it is eternal, then either it is described with perfect attributes or not. If it is not described with perfect attributes, then it is not eternal, because being devoid of perfect attributes necessitates being described with their opposites, all of which are imperfections—this is a sign of originatedness. If it is described with perfect attributes and takwin subsists in it, then it is the creator of the world and its maker, not that other [being]. And from this comes what we have maintained, and you have refused to affirm an eternal maker of the world for whom takwin is an attribute subsisting in Him, and all your efforts are nullified. After that, the claim of affirming another eternal [being] that has no [attributes] is invalid, because affirming two eternals subsisting in essence is impossible as we have said. Likewise, making one who has perfect attributes and is described with takwin not the maker of the world, and making one who has no [such attributes] the maker, is to invert reason, so it is false. And if that locus is originated, then either it occurred by a takwin or it occurred without a takwin. If it occurred without a takwin, then either it occurred [without meaning] from the Eternal [i.e., without divine agency] or it occurred by power. There is no way to say it occurred without meaning from the Eternal, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, and this involves negation of the Maker. And there is no way to say it occurred by power without a takwin, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, and takwin would be entirely nullified; then the world would be an object of power of Allah, not His creation, and Allah would be powerful over the world but not its creator. To say this is disbelief, because power does not entail existence without the act, so this also involves negation of the Maker. And because if its existence were by power, then power would be an act of causing existence, so it would be pre-eternally causing existence. And if it occurred by a takwin, then either it occurred by a prior takwin—as is narrated from Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir—or it occurred by a concurrent takwin—as is narrated from Abu al-Hudhayl. If it occurred by a prior takwin, then takwin would not subsist in it before its existence, because the subsistence of an existent takwin in a non-existent locus is impossible; and we have already refuted the self-subsistence of takwin. And because if it is possible for takwin to exist without a locus for one time, it is possible for many times, since there is no difference between precedence by one time and precedence by many times regarding the possibility of its existence without a locus. And if so, their claim that the existence of takwin necessarily necessitates the existence of the locus and that it cannot precede it is refuted. We will explain this more fully in the question of capacity (al-istita'a), God willing.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the possibility that the attribute of creating (takwin) could subsist in a locus other than God's essence. The author divides the opponents' hypothetical claim into two main possibilities: either takwin subsists in a locus (which is not God), or it subsists without a locus (already refuted). Here he tackles the first possibility. He provides three reasons.

First reason: The regress argument mentioned earlier—if takwin occurs by a takwin, then infinite regress, etc. (summarized, as previously established).

Second reason: If takwin subsists in a locus, then that locus would be the true creator, not God. This is because the attribute of creating must inhere in the agent; if it inheres in another, that other becomes the agent.

Third reason: The locus in which takwin subsists must be either eternal or originated.

- If eternal: The locus must either possess perfect attributes (like God's) or not. If it lacks perfect attributes, it cannot be eternal (since lack of perfection is a sign of originatedness). If it does have perfect attributes and contains takwin, then it is the creator—not God. Thus, the opponent either ends up affirming another eternal being (which is absurd in many ways) or denying God's role as creator.

- If originated: The originated locus itself must have come into existence either by a takwin or without one. Each branch is examined and shown to lead to absurdity:
  - If without a takwin: Either from the Eternal (with no meaning) or by power. The first would allow the entire world to come about without divine agency (negation of God). The second would make the world merely an object of power, not creation—implying God is not a creator, which is disbelief. Also, power does not entail existence.
  - If by a takwin: The takwin could be prior or concurrent. If prior, then takwin would subsist in the locus before its existence—impossible. Also, if takwin can precede its locus by one time, it can precede by many times, refuting the claim that takwin necessarily implies its locus. If concurrent, the argument is bundled?

The passage concludes with a brief dismissal of the concurrent view (by implication) and refers to fuller treatment elsewhere. The author systematically closes every logical avenue for takwin to be attributed to a locus other than God, firmly establishing that takwin must be an attribute subsisting in God's essence.

Key Terms
تكوين
محل
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think takwin can be an accident in a separate substance, like an attribute inhering in a non-God entity.
Correction: The second reason shows that the attribute's locus is the agent itself. If takwin were in another locus, that locus would be the creator, which contradicts the opponent's own theology.

Checkpoint
According to the second reason, if takwin subsists in a locus other than God, who would be the creator of the world?
A) God
B) The locus in which takwin subsists
C) No one
D) Both God and the locus

Key Takeaway
Takwin cannot subsist in another locus because that would either cause regress or misassign agency to something other than God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself attributing the good changes in your life to your own skill, to a system, or to another person, forgetting that both the means and the outcome are solely from God? How can you train your heart to see every act of creation as directly from Him?
?
When you pray for something and it happens, do you immediately think 'my dua worked' or do you remember that takwin belongs only to Allah? What would it look like to actually live as if He alone brings things into being, without any independent secondary cause?
?
If you truly believe that no attribute of creation can reside in anyone but Allah, how does that change the way you view people who seem powerful or influential? Will you still fear them or rely on them as if they have independent creative power?
