The Third Reason: If the Locus of Takwin is Eternal
Imam Nasafi refutes the possibility of an eternal locus for takwin, showing it leads to absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an eternal locus for takwin is impossible, leading to either denying its eternality or affirming a second creator.

Core Idea
An eternal locus for takwin either lacks perfection (so not eternal) or has it (so is the creator, not God).

Imam Nasafi now examines the scenario where the locus of takwin is claimed to be eternal. He splits this into two subcases: either that eternal locus possesses perfect attributes or it does not. Both lead to contradictions with the opponent's own claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the two subcases. Then read the translation.
Note the conditional structure: 'if it is eternal, then either it is described with perfect attributes or not'.
2
Analyze the first subcase
If the eternal locus lacks perfect attributes, it cannot be eternal because lacking perfection is a sign of originatedness.
The author argues that absence of perfect attributes implies opposite imperfections, which indicate contingency.
3
Analyze the second subcase
If the eternal locus has perfect attributes and contains takwin, then it is the creator, not God. This leads to affirming another eternal creator, which is impossible.
The author also points out that this inverts reason: making the one with perfection not the creator, and the one without it the creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حدوثه في محل آخر سوى ذات القديم فمحال فاسد أيضا لوجوه: أحدها بما مر من أن التكوين حدث بتكوين أم لا بتكوين إلى آخر ما بينا. والثاني أن التكوين لو كان قائما بمحل لكان المكون للعالم من قام به التكوين لا الله تعالى وقد قررنا الصفات التي مر ذكرها أن الموصوف محالها لا غيرها كما في جميع ذلك غير مرة. والثالث أن ذلك المحل الذي قام به التكوين إما أن يكون قديما وإما أن يكون محدثا، فإن كان قديما إما أن كان موصوفا بصفات الكمال وإما أن لم يكن موصوفا بها، فإن لم يكن موصوفا بها فلا يكون قديما، إذ التعري عن صفات الكمال يوجب الاتصاف بأضدادها وهي كلها نقائص وذلك من أمارات الحدوث، ولو كان موصوفا بصفات الكمال والتكوين قائم به فهو الخالق للعالم المكون له لا ذلك الغير. وجاء من هذا ما ذهبنا إليه وأبيتم أنتم من إثبات صانع قديم للعالم كان التكوين صفة له قائمة به وبطل جميع سعيكم. فبعد ذلك القول بإثبات قديم آخر لا تكون له باطل، إذ القول بالقديمين القائمين بالذات محال على ما مر. وكذلك جعل من له صفات الكمال وهو موصوف بالتكوين غير صانع للعالم، وجعل من لا تكون له صانعا له قلب المعقول فيكون باطلا. وإن كان ذلك المحل حادثا إما أن حدث بتكوين وإما أن حدث لا بتكوين. فإن حدث لا بتكوين، فإما أن حدث لا بمعنى من قبل الباري وإما أن حدث بالقدرة، ولا وجه إلى القول بحدوثه لا بمعنى من قبل الباري لأنه لو جاز ذلك فيه لجاز في جميع العالم وفيه تعطيل الصانع، ولا وجه للقول بحدوثه بالقدرة لا بتكوين لما مر أنه لو جاز هذا فيه لجاز في جميع العالم فبطل التكوين أصلا، فيكون العالم مقدور الله تعالى لا مخلوقه، ويكون الله قادرا على العالم لا خالقا له، والقول به كفر لما أن القدرة لا تقتضى الوجود بدون الفعل، فيكون فيه أيضا تعطيل الصانع. ولأن وجوده لو كان بالقدرة لكانت القدرة إيجادا وهي فكان الإيجاد أزنيا. ولو حدث بتكوين إما أن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه كما هو المحكي عن بشر بن المعتمر، وإما أن حدث بتكوين مقارن له كما هو المحكي عن أبي الهذيل، فإن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه فإذا لا قيام للتكوين به قبل وجوده إذ قيام تكوين موجود بمكون لم يوجد بعد محال، وقد أبطلنا قيام التكوين بنفسه، ولأنه لما جاز وجود التكوين ولا مكون بعد زمانا واحدا جاز أزمنة كثيرة إذ لا فرق بين التقدم بزمان والتقدم بأزمنة في أن وجوده ولا مكون جائز. وإذا كان كذلك بطل ادعاؤهم أن وجود التكوين يقتضي وجود المكون لا محالة ولا يجوز سبقه عليه ونبين هذا بأتم من ذلك في مسألة الاستطاعة إن شاء الله تعالى.
As for its occurrence in another locus besides the Eternal Essence, it is also impossible and corrupt, for reasons: One of them is what has already passed—that takwin occurred either by a takwin or not by a takwin, etc., up to what we explained. Second, that if takwin were subsisting in a locus, then the maker of the world would be the one in whom takwin subsists, not Allah; and we have established the attributes mentioned earlier, that the described thing's locus is its own, not another's, as we have repeatedly shown. Third, that locus in which takwin subsists is either eternal or originated. If it is eternal, then either it is described with perfect attributes or not. If it is not described with perfect attributes, then it is not eternal, because being devoid of perfect attributes necessitates being described with their opposites, all of which are imperfections—this is a sign of originatedness. If it is described with perfect attributes and takwin subsists in it, then it is the creator of the world and its maker, not that other [being]. And from this comes what we have maintained, and you have refused to affirm an eternal maker of the world for whom takwin is an attribute subsisting in Him, and all your efforts are nullified. After that, the claim of affirming another eternal [being] that has no [attributes] is invalid, because affirming two eternals subsisting in essence is impossible as we have said. Likewise, making one who has perfect attributes and is described with takwin not the maker of the world, and making one who has no [such attributes] the maker, is to invert reason, so it is false. And if that locus is originated, then either it occurred by a takwin or it occurred without a takwin. If it occurred without a takwin, then either it occurred [without meaning] from the Eternal [i.e., without divine agency] or it occurred by power. There is no way to say it occurred without meaning from the Eternal, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, and this involves negation of the Maker. And there is no way to say it occurred by power without a takwin, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, and takwin would be entirely nullified; then the world would be an object of power of Allah, not His creation, and Allah would be powerful over the world but not its creator. To say this is disbelief, because power does not entail existence without the act, so this also involves negation of the Maker. And because if its existence were by power, then power would be an act of causing existence, so it would be pre-eternally causing existence. And if it occurred by a takwin, then either it occurred by a prior takwin—as is narrated from Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir—or it occurred by a concurrent takwin—as is narrated from Abu al-Hudhayl. If it occurred by a prior takwin, then takwin would not subsist in it before its existence, because the subsistence of an existent takwin in a non-existent locus is impossible; and we have already refuted the self-subsistence of takwin. And because if it is possible for takwin to exist without a locus for one time, it is possible for many times, since there is no difference between precedence by one time and precedence by many times regarding the possibility of its existence without a locus. And if so, their claim that the existence of takwin necessarily necessitates the existence of the locus and that it cannot precede it is refuted. We will explain this more fully in the question of capacity (al-istita'a), God willing.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the possibility that the attribute of creating (takwin) could subsist in a locus other than God's essence. The author divides the opponents' hypothetical claim into two main possibilities: either takwin subsists in a locus (which is not God), or it subsists without a locus (already refuted). Here he tackles the first possibility. He provides three reasons.

First reason: The regress argument mentioned earlier—if takwin occurs by a takwin, then infinite regress, etc. (summarized, as previously established).

Second reason: If takwin subsists in a locus, then that locus would be the true creator, not God. This is because the attribute of creating must inhere in the agent; if it inheres in another, that other becomes the agent.

Third reason: The locus in which takwin subsists must be either eternal or originated.

- If eternal: The locus must either possess perfect attributes (like God's) or not. If it lacks perfect attributes, it cannot be eternal (since lack of perfection is a sign of originatedness). If it does have perfect attributes and contains takwin, then it is the creator—not God. Thus, the opponent either ends up affirming another eternal being (which is absurd in many ways) or denying God's role as creator.

- If originated: The originated locus itself must have come into existence either by a takwin or without one. Each branch is examined and shown to lead to absurdity:
  - If without a takwin: Either from the Eternal (with no meaning) or by power. The first would allow the entire world to come about without divine agency (negation of God). The second would make the world merely an object of power, not creation—implying God is not a creator, which is disbelief. Also, power does not entail existence.
  - If by a takwin: The takwin could be prior or concurrent. If prior, then takwin would subsist in the locus before its existence—impossible. Also, if takwin can precede its locus by one time, it can precede by many times, refuting the claim that takwin necessarily implies its locus. If concurrent, the argument is bundled?

The passage concludes with a brief dismissal of the concurrent view (by implication) and refers to fuller treatment elsewhere. The author systematically closes every logical avenue for takwin to be attributed to a locus other than God, firmly establishing that takwin must be an attribute subsisting in God's essence.

Key Terms
قديم
صفات الكمال
تعطيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think an eternal being can exist without perfect attributes, like a neutral eternal substance.
Correction: The author argues that lacking perfect attributes implies having their opposites (imperfections), which is a sign of originatedness, contradicting eternality.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude if the eternal locus has perfect attributes and contains takwin?
A) It is God
B) It is the creator of the world
C) It is impossible
D) It is a partner to God

Key Takeaway
An eternal locus for takwin cannot be devoid of perfection, and if it has perfection, it becomes the creator—not God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed creation power to any being or cause other than Allah, even indirectly? This argument demands that you examine whether anything in your life holds an 'eternal' or 'independent' status in your heart. Is there any created thing you treat as if it has ultimate control over your outcomes?
?
If you truly believe that only a perfect eternal being can create, how does that affect the way you rely on Allah versus your own efforts? Are there areas where you act as if you are the independent 'creator' of your own success?
?
This passage refutes the possibility of an eternal imperfect locus. What does that tell you about the absolute perfection of Allah? How does that confront any casual or irreverent thoughts you have about God's attributes?

Originated Locus Without Takwin
Imam Nasafi refutes the possibility of an originated locus for takwin coming into existence without a takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an originated locus for takwin cannot come into existence without a takwin, as that leads to negation of God's role as creator.

Core Idea
An originated locus without takwin implies either a world without divine agency or a mere power that does not create.

Imam Nasafi continues the third reason by considering the case where the locus of takwin is itself originated. He first examines the branch where it occurs without a takwin. He splits this into two sub-branches: either it occurs without any meaning from the Eternal (i.e., without divine agency) or it occurs by power alone. Both lead to absurdities or disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two subcases: 'without meaning from the Eternal' and 'by power'.
The language is dense; take your time with the translation.
2
Analyze the first subcase
If the locus occurs without any meaning or agency from God, then the whole world could come about without God, which negates the Maker.
The author uses the principle of 'what is permissible for one is permissible for all' (analogy).
3
Analyze the second subcase
If the locus occurs by power alone (without takwin), then everything could come about by power, rendering takwin meaningless. This implies God is powerful but not a creator, which is disbelief because power does not entail existence without an act.
The author argues that this also leads to negation of the Maker.

التكوين لا الله تعالى وقد قررنا الصفات التي مر ذكرها أن الموصوف محالها لا غيرها كما في جميع ذلك غير مرة. والثالث أن ذلك المحل الذي قام به التكوين إما أن يكون قديما وإما أن يكون محدثا، فإن كان قديما بتكوين إما أن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه كما هو المحكي عن بشر بن المعتمر، وإما أن حدث بتكوين مقارن له كما هو المحكي عن أبي الهذيل، فإن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه فإذا لا قيام للتكوين به قبل وجوده إذ قيام تكوين As for its occurrence in another locus besides the Eternal Essence, it is also impossible and corrupt, for reasons: One of them is what has already passed—that takwin occurred either by a takwin or not by a takwin, etc., up to what we explained. Second, that if takwin were subsisting in a locus, then the maker of the world would be the one in whom takwin subsists, not Allah; and we have established the attributes mentioned earlier, that the described thing's locus is its own, not another's, as we have repeatedly shown. Third, that locus in which takwin subsists is either eternal or originated. If it is eternal, then either it is described with perfect attributes or not. If it is not described with perfect attributes, then it is not eternal, because being devoid of perfect attributes necessitates being described with their opposites, all of which are imperfections—this is a sign of originatedness. If it is described with perfect attributes and takwin subsists in it, then it is the creator of the world and its maker, not that other [being]. And from this comes what we have maintained, and you have refused to affirm an eternal maker of the world for whom takwin is an attribute subsisting in Him, and all your efforts are nullified. After that, the claim of affirming another eternal [being] that has no [attributes] is invalid, because affirming two eternals subsisting in essence is impossible as we have said. Likewise, making one who has perfect attributes and is described with takwin not the maker of the world, and making one who has no [such attributes] the maker, is to invert reason, so it is false. And if that locus is originated, then either it occurred by a takwin or it occurred without a takwin. If it occurred without a takwin, then either it occurred [without meaning] from the Eternal [i.e., without divine agency] or it occurred by power. There is no way to say it occurred without meaning from the Eternal, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, and this involves negation of the Maker. And there is no way to say it occurred by power without a takwin, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, and takwin would be entirely nullified; then the world would be an object of power of Allah, not His creation, and Allah would be powerful over the world but not its creator. To say this is disbelief, because power does not entail existence without the act, so this also involves negation of the Maker. And because if its existence were by power, then power would be an act of causing existence, so it would be pre-eternally causing existence. And if it occurred by a takwin, then either it occurred by a prior takwin—as is narrated from Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir—or it occurred by a concurrent takwin—as is narrated from Abu al-Hudhayl. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's power alone is sufficient to create without an act of creation (takwin).
Correction: The author argues that power without an act does not bring existence; otherwise, the entire world would be merely an object of power, not creation, which is disbelief. Takwin is the act that brings existence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what follows if the locus occurs by power without a takwin?
A) The world is God's creation
B) The world is an object of God's power but not His creation
C) Takwin becomes necessary
D) God becomes a creator

Key Takeaway
An originated locus for takwin cannot come into existence without a takwin, as that undermines God's role as creator and is tantamount to disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever think, even for a moment, that God's power alone is sufficient to bring things into existence without His specific act of creation? What does this passage reveal about the danger of that thought—for your own belief in God as Creator? Will you correct this in your heart?
?
If you believe that something could come into existence without divine agency, even in a single case, how does this argument show that you are threatening the very concept of God as Maker? Are you willing to examine your own assumptions about God's role in the events of your life?
?
This passage equates the idea of power without act to disbelief. Have you ever casually attributed events to 'just happening' or 'fate' without explicitly acknowledging God's creative act behind them? What does this call you to change in how you speak of everyday occurrences?

Originated Locus By a Prior Takwin
Imam Nasafi refutes the possibility of an originated locus coming into existence by a prior takwin, showing it leads to logical contradictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an originated locus for takwin cannot come into existence by a prior takwin, as that leads to the contradiction of takwin subsisting before its locus.

Core Idea
If takwin precedes its locus, it would exist without a locus, which is impossible; this refutes the claim that takwin necessitates its locus.

Imam Nasafi now examines the final branch where the originated locus occurs by a takwin. He considers two views: the takwin being prior (as held by Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir) or concurrent (as held by Abu al-Hudhayl). He focuses on the prior takwin view, showing it leads to absurdities such as takwin existing without a locus and the possibility of indefinite delay.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that the passage focuses on the prior takwin view, referencing Bishr and Abu al-Hudhayl.
The author briefly mentions the concurrent view but does not elaborate here.
2
Understand the first problem
If takwin is prior to the locus, it would have to subsist in the locus before the locus exists, which is impossible because an accident cannot subsist in a non-existent subject.
The author also references a previous refutation that takwin cannot subsist in itself.
3
Understand the second problem
If takwin can exist without a locus for one time, it can for many times, contradicting the claim that takwin necessarily implies its locus.
This refutes the opponent's contention that takwin always accompanies its locus.

Source Text

بإثبات قديم آخر لا تكون له باطل، إذ القول بالقديمين القائمين بالذات محال على ما مر. وكذلك جعل من له صفات الكمال وهو موصوف بالتكوين غير صانع للعالم، وجعل من لا تكون له صانعا له قلب المعقول فيكون باطلا. وإن كان ذلك المحل حادثا إما أن حدث بتكوين وإما أن حدث لا بتكوين. فإن حدث لا بتكوين، فإما أن حدث لا بمعنى من قبل الباري وإما أن حدث بالقدرة، ولا وجه إلى القول بحدوثه لا بمعنى من قبل الباري لأنه لو جاز ذلك فيه لجاز في جميع العالم وفيه تعطيل الصانع، ولا وجه للقول بحدوثه بالقدرة لا بتكوين لما مر أنه لو جاز هذا فيه لجاز في جميع العالم فبطل التكوين أصلا، فيكون العالم مقدور الله تعالى لا مخلوقه، ويكون الله قادرا على العالم لا خالقا له، والقول به كفر لما أن القدرة لا تقتضى الوجود بدون الفعل، فيكون فيه أيضا تعطيل الصانع. ولأن وجوده لو كان بالقدرة لكانت القدرة إيجادا وهي فكان الإيجاد أزنيا. ولو حدث بتكوين إما أن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه كما هو المحكي عن بشر بن المعتمر، وإما أن حدث بتكوين مقارن له كما هو المحكي عن أبي الهذيل، فإن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه فإذا لا قيام للتكوين به قبل وجوده إذ قيام تكوين موجود بمكون لم يوجد بعد محال، وقد أبطلنا قيام التكوين بنفسه، ولأنه لما جاز وجود التكوين ولا مكون بعد زمانا واحدا جاز أزمنة كثيرة إذ لا فرق بين التقدم بزمان والتقدم بأزمنة في أن وجوده ولا مكون جائز. وإذا كان كذلك بطل ادعاؤهم أن وجود التكوين يقتضي وجود المكون لا محالة ولا يجوز سبقه عليه ونبين هذا بأتم من ذلك في مسألة الاستطاعة إن شاء الله تعالى.
As for its occurrence in another locus besides the Eternal Essence, it is also impossible and corrupt, for reasons: One of them is what has already passed—that takwin occurred either by a takwin or not by a takwin, etc., up to what we explained. Second, that if takwin were subsisting in a locus, then the maker of the world would be the one in whom takwin subsists, not Allah; and we have established the attributes mentioned earlier, that the described thing's locus is its own, not another's, as we have repeatedly shown. Third, that locus in which takwin subsists is either eternal or originated. If it is eternal, then either it is described with perfect attributes or not. If it is not described with perfect attributes, then it is not eternal, because being devoid of perfect attributes necessitates being described with their opposites, all of which are imperfections—this is a sign of originatedness. If it is described with perfect attributes and takwin subsists in it, then it is the creator of the world and its maker, not that other [being]. And from this comes what we have maintained, and you have refused to affirm an eternal maker of the world for whom takwin is an attribute subsisting in Him, and all your efforts are nullified. After that, the claim of affirming another eternal [being] that has no [attributes] is invalid, because affirming two eternals subsisting in essence is impossible as we have said. Likewise, making one who has perfect attributes and is described with takwin not the maker of the world, and making one who has no [such attributes] the maker, is to invert reason, so it is false. And if that locus is originated, then either it occurred by a takwin or it occurred without a takwin. If it occurred without a takwin, then either it occurred [without meaning] from the Eternal [i.e., without divine agency] or it occurred by power. There is no way to say it occurred without meaning from the Eternal, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, and this involves negation of the Maker. And there is no way to say it occurred by power without a takwin, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, and takwin would be entirely nullified; then the world would be an object of power of Allah, not His creation, and Allah would be powerful over the world but not its creator. To say this is disbelief, because power does not entail existence without the act, so this also involves negation of the Maker. And because if its existence were by power, then power would be an act of causing existence, so it would be pre-eternally causing existence. And if it occurred by a takwin, then either it occurred by a prior takwin—as is narrated from Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir—or it occurred by a concurrent takwin—as is narrated from Abu al-Hudhayl. If it occurred by a prior takwin, then takwin would not subsist in it before its existence, because the subsistence of an existent takwin in a non-existent locus is impossible; and we have already refuted the self-subsistence of takwin. And because if it is possible for takwin to exist without a locus for one time, it is possible for many times, since there is no difference between precedence by one time and precedence by many times regarding the possibility of its existence without a locus. And if so, their claim that the existence of takwin necessarily necessitates the existence of the locus and that it cannot precede it is refuted. We will explain this more fully in the question of capacity (al-istita'a), God willing.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the possibility that the attribute of creating (takwin) could subsist in a locus other than God's essence. The author divides the opponents' hypothetical claim into two main possibilities: either takwin subsists in a locus (which is not God), or it subsists without a locus (already refuted). Here he tackles the first possibility. He provides three reasons.

First reason: The regress argument mentioned earlier—if takwin occurs by a takwin, then infinite regress, etc. (summarized, as previously established).

Second reason: If takwin subsists in a locus, then that locus would be the true creator, not God. This is because the attribute of creating must inhere in the agent; if it inheres in another, that other becomes the agent.

Third reason: The locus in which takwin subsists must be either eternal or originated.

- If eternal: The locus must either possess perfect attributes (like God's) or not. If it lacks perfect attributes, it cannot be eternal (since lack of perfection is a sign of originatedness). If it does have perfect attributes and contains takwin, then it is the creator—not God. Thus, the opponent either ends up affirming another eternal being (which is absurd in many ways) or denying God's role as creator.

- If originated: The originated locus itself must have come into existence either by a takwin or without one. Each branch is examined and shown to lead to absurdity:
  - If without a takwin: Either from the Eternal (with no meaning) or by power. The first would allow the entire world to come about without divine agency (negation of God). The second would make the world merely an object of power, not creation—implying God is not a creator, which is disbelief. Also, power does not entail existence.
  - If by a takwin: The takwin could be prior or concurrent. If prior, then takwin would subsist in the locus before its existence—impossible. Also, if takwin can precede its locus by one time, it can precede by many times, refuting the claim that takwin necessarily implies its locus. If concurrent, the argument is bundled?

The passage concludes with a brief dismissal of the concurrent view (by implication) and refers to fuller treatment elsewhere. The author systematically closes every logical avenue for takwin to be attributed to a locus other than God, firmly establishing that takwin must be an attribute subsisting in God's essence.

Key Terms
تكوين
محل
بشر بن المعتمر
أبو الهذيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that takwin can precede its locus without issue, as a cause precedes its effect.
Correction: The author argues that takwin is an accident that requires a locus; existing before the locus is impossible. If it could, it would break the necessary connection claimed by opponents.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if takwin can exist without a locus for one time?
A) It proves takwin is eternal
B) It can exist without a locus for many times
C) It forces the locus to exist immediately
D) It shows takwin is not an attribute

Key Takeaway
An originated locus cannot be produced by a prior takwin, as that would require takwin to exist without a locus, which is impossible and refutes the opponent's claim of necessary concomitance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your beliefs, are you willing to follow logic to its conclusion even if it dismantles a comfortable assumption? What in your life have you assumed 'must be' a certain way without considering the logical basis?
?
The author argues that if something is possible in one moment, it is possible in many. Are there any small compromises in your faith or practice that you allow 'just this once' that could logically lead to a pattern of many?
?
This passage demands rigorous consistency. Where in your relationship with Allah have you accepted contradictions—believing in His power yet acting as if causes operate independently? How can you align your heart with the logical implications of tawhid?

Rejecting a Pre-eternal Locus for Takwin
Opens with a dual refutation of a pre-eternal locus for takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why takwin cannot have a pre-eternal locus and how this preserves tawhid.

Core Idea
If takwin had a pre-eternal locus, there would be two pre-eternals—impossible.

The author begins by declaring the impossibility of takwin having a locus. He first tackles the possibility of a pre-eternal locus, showing that it would imply two eternal beings subsisting in God's essence, which is rationally impossible. Then he argues that denying takwin to the one who has all attributes of perfection (i.e., God) would absurdly make Him not the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage slowly
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the two distinct arguments: one about two pre-eternals, one about the consequence of denying takwin to God.
The second argument is a rhetorical reductio.
2
Identify the two premises
First premise: if takwin has a pre-eternal locus, there are two pre-eternals (God and the locus). Second premise: if God has takwin but is not the maker, absurdity arises.
3
Understand 'قلب المعقول'
The phrase 'overturns reason' means the conclusion is intellectually unacceptable. Why would it be absurd to say God has takwin but is not the Creator?
Because takwin is precisely the act of bringing into existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكون له باطل، إذ القول بالقديمين القائمين بالذات محال على ما مر. وكذلك جعل له من له صفات الكمال وهو موصوف بالتكوين غير صانع للعالم، وجعل من لا تكون له صانعا له قلب المعقول فيكون باطلا. وإن كان ذلك المحل حادثا إما أن حدث بتكوين وإما أن حدث لا بتكوين. فإن حدث لا بتكوين، فإما أن حدث لا بمعنى من قبل الباري، وإما أن حدث بالقدرة، ولا وجه إلى القول بحدوثه لا بمعنى من قبل الباري لأنه لو جاز ذلك فيه لجاز في جميع العالم وفيه تعطيل الصانع، ولا وجه للقول بحدوثه بالقدرة لا بتكوين لما مر أنه لو جاز هذا فيه لجاز في جميع العالم فبطل التكوين أصلا، فيكون العالم مقدور الله تعالى لا مخلوقه، ويكون الله قادرا على العالم لا خالقا له، والقول به كفر لما أن القدرة لا تقتضى الوجود بدون الفعل، فيكون فيه أيضا تعطيل الصانع. ولأن وجوده لو كان بالقدرة لكانت القدرة إيجادا وهي فكان الإيجاد أزليا. ولو حدث بتكوين إما أن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه كما هو المحكي عن بشر بن المعتمر، وإما أن حدث بتكوين مقارن له كما هو المحكي عن أبي الهذيل، فإن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه فإذا لا قيام للتكوين به قبل وجوده إذ قيام تكوين موجود بمكون لم يوجد بعد محال، وقد أبطلنا قيام التكوين بنفسه، ولأنه لما جاز وجود التكوين ولا مكون بعد زمانا واحدا جاز أزمنة كثيرة إذ لا فرق بين التقدم بزمان والتقدم بأزمنة في أن وجوده ولا مكون جائز . وإذا كان كذلك بطل ادعاؤهم – أن وجود التكوين يقتضي وجود المكون لا محالة ولا يجوز سبقه عليه ـ ونبين هذا بأتم من ذلك في مسألة الاستطاعة – إن شاء الله تعالى. ولو كان التكوين مقارنا له فلم يكن على أصلهم إضافة وجود المكون إلى التكوين أولى من إضافة وجود التكوين إلى المكون كما يشنعون علينا في مسألة الاستطاعة مع الفعل، فإما أن يترك أبو الهذيل ذلك التشنيع وينقاد للحق، وإما أن يترك هذا القول. وإلا فهو مناقض . ونقول له أيضا ، لما كان التكوين قائما بالمكون فالمكون إذا هو المكون لنفسه لما مر أن الموصوف بالصفة من قام به لا من لم يقم به، فيكون العالم على هذا خالقا لنفسه وفيه أمران أحدهما تعطيل الصانع وهو كفر، والثاني إيجاد الشيء نفسه وهو محال على ما مر في باب إثبات الصانع.
It is false, because the assertion of two pre-eternals subsisting in the Essence is impossible as previously mentioned. Likewise, making one who has attributes of perfection and is described by takwin (bringing into existence) not the maker of the world, and making one who does not have takwin the maker of it, overturns reason and is false. If that locus is originated, either it occurs by takwin or it occurs not by takwin. If it occurs not by takwin, then either it occurs without a meaning from the Creator, or it occurs by power (al-qudra). There is no way to say it occurs without a meaning from the Creator, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world and that would entail the suspension (taʿṭīl) of the Maker. And there is no way to say it occurs by power without takwin, because as previously mentioned, if this were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, so takwin would be nullified entirely. Thus the world would be something God has power over but not His creation, and God would be powerful over the world but not its Creator. Holding this is unbelief (kufr), because power (al-qudra) does not necessitate existence without the act. So this also entails the suspension of the Maker. And because if its existence were by power, then power would be bringing into existence (ījād), and bringing into existence would be eternal. If it occurs by takwin, either it occurs by a takwin prior to it, as narrated from Bishr ibn al-Muʿtamir, or it occurs by a takwin concomitant with it, as narrated from Abū l-Hudhayl. If it occurs by a takwin prior to it, then takwin cannot subsist in it before its existence, because the subsistence of an existing takwin in something not yet existing is impossible. And we have already refuted the subsistence of takwin in itself. And because if it is permissible for takwin to exist without that which is brought into existence (al-mukawwan) for one time, it is permissible for many times, since there is no difference between priority by one time and priority by many times in that its existence without that which is brought into existence is permissible. If this is so, their claim is refuted—that the existence of takwin necessarily entails the existence of the brought into existence and that priority over it is not permissible. We will explain this more fully in the question of capacity (al-istiṭāʿa), God willing. If takwin were concomitant with it, then according to their principle, attributing the existence of the brought into existence to takwin is no more appropriate than attributing the existence of takwin to the brought into existence, just as they argue against us in the question of capacity (al-istiṭāʿa) with the act. So either Abū l-Hudhayl abandons that argument and submits to the truth, or he abandons this statement. Otherwise he is contradictory. We also say to him: since takwin subsists in the brought into existence, then the brought into existence is the bringer into existence of itself, because as previously mentioned, the one described by an attribute is the one in which it subsists, not the one in which it does not subsist. Thus on this view the world would be the creator of itself, and there are two issues: first, the suspension of the Maker, which is unbelief; second, the bringing of a thing into existence by itself, which is impossible as previously mentioned in the chapter on establishing the Maker.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that takwin (bringing into existence) can have a locus (maḥall), whether that locus is pre-eternal or originated. The author (al-Nasafī) argues that takwin cannot be an attribute separate from God because it would lead to absurdities. He systematically considers two possibilities: the locus is pre-eternal or originated. If the locus is pre-eternal, that would imply two pre-eternals, which is impossible. If the locus is originated, it either occurs by takwin or not. If not by takwin, it must be by power (qudra), but this would mean the world is merely a possible thing (maqdūr) not a created thing (makhluq), leading to kufr. If by takwin, the takwin is either prior to or simultaneous with the locus. Prior takwin is impossible because takwin cannot subsist in a non-existent. Simultaneous takwin leads to a contradiction: the locus would be self-creating, which is impossible. Thus the argument concludes that takwin is not a separate attribute but identical with God's creative act.

Key Terms
التكوين
المحل
القديم
الصانع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think takwin could be an attribute that inheres in a separate pre-eternal entity co-existing with God.
Correction: This would imply two eternal beings, violating the oneness of God; also, it separates the attribute from its effect, making God not the actual Creator.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about making someone who has takwin not the maker of the world?
A) It is a valid interpretation.
B) It overthrows reason and is false.
C) It is permissible if the locus is pre-eternal.
D) It is the view of the Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
Takwin cannot have a pre-eternal locus because it would either imply two pre-eternals or absurdly deny God's role as Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever conceive of God's attributes as separate 'parts' or powers in your mind? How does the oneness of God demand that His attributes are inseparable from His essence? Examine your own understanding: do you truly believe God is one in every sense, or do you sometimes imagine attributes as multiple 'things' in Him? This lesson calls you to purify your tawhid.
?
If you believe God has the power to create (takwin), do you also truly believe He is the sole Creator of everything, including your daily actions and successes? Where do you subtly attribute creative power to others—your own effort, luck, or people? The passage shows that separating takwin from creation is 'overturning reason'. Have you ever done that in your heart?
?
The passage forcefully rejects any second pre-eternal entity. Is there anything in your life you treat as co-eternal or independent of God—a habit, a person, a pursuit? Repent and realign your heart to see God's sole pre-eternality and absolute creative power in every moment.

Originated Locus Without Takwin: Power and Ta'til
Refutes the possibility of an originated locus occurring not by takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a originated locus for takwin cannot come about without takwin itself, and how the alternatives lead to kufr or ta'til.

Core Idea
If the locus occurs without takwin, either by power or without meaning, it leads to suspension of the Creator.

Having dismissed a pre-eternal locus, the author now considers an originated locus. He splits the case into two: either the locus occurs by takwin or not. Here he examines the 'not by takwin' branch, which itself has two subcases: occurring without a meaning from the Creator, or occurring by power (qudra). Both, he argues, are impossible and lead to disastrous theological consequences.

Guided Path
1
Follow the branching logic
Notice the tree: originated locus → either by takwin or not. Focus on 'not by takwin' branch.
The 'by takwin' branch will come later.
2
Evaluate the first subcase: without a meaning from the Creator
If the locus occurs without any meaning (cause) from God, then the same could happen for the entire world, leading to ta'til (suspension of the Creator).
Ta'til means denying God's role as Creator.
3
Evaluate the second subcase: by power (qudra) without takwin
If the locus occurs by power alone, then the world would be merely something God has power over, not His creation. This would make God a 'powerful being' but not a 'creator', which is kufr.
Power does not necessitate existence without the act of bringing into existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكون له باطل، إذ القول بالقديمين القائمين بالذات محال على ما مر. وكذلك جعل له من له صفات الكمال وهو موصوف بالتكوين غير صانع للعالم، وجعل من لا تكون له صانعا له قلب المعقول فيكون باطلا. وإن كان ذلك المحل حادثا إما أن حدث بتكوين وإما أن حدث لا بتكوين. فإن حدث لا بتكوين، فإما أن حدث لا بمعنى من قبل الباري، وإما أن حدث بالقدرة، ولا وجه إلى القول بحدوثه لا بمعنى من قبل الباري لأنه لو جاز ذلك فيه لجاز في جميع العالم وفيه تعطيل الصانع، ولا وجه للقول بحدوثه بالقدرة لا بتكوين لما مر أنه لو جاز هذا فيه لجاز في جميع العالم فبطل التكوين أصلا، فيكون العالم مقدور الله تعالى لا مخلوقه، ويكون الله قادرا على العالم لا خالقا له، والقول به كفر لما أن القدرة لا تقتضى الوجود بدون الفعل، فيكون فيه أيضا تعطيل الصانع. ولأن وجوده لو كان بالقدرة لكانت القدرة إيجادا وهي فكان الإيجاد أزليا. ولو حدث بتكوين إما أن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه كما هو المحكي عن بشر بن المعتمر، وإما أن حدث بتكوين مقارن له كما هو المحكي عن أبي الهذيل، فإن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه فإذا لا قيام للتكوين به قبل وجوده إذ قيام تكوين موجود بمكون لم يوجد بعد محال، وقد أبطلنا قيام التكوين بنفسه، ولأنه لما جاز وجود التكوين ولا مكون بعد زمانا واحدا جاز أزمنة كثيرة إذ لا فرق بين التقدم بزمان والتقدم بأزمنة في أن وجوده ولا مكون جائز . وإذا كان كذلك بطل ادعاؤهم – أن وجود التكوين يقتضي وجود المكون لا محالة ولا يجوز سبقه عليه ـ ونبين هذا بأتم من ذلك في مسألة الاستطاعة – إن شاء الله تعالى. ولو كان التكوين مقارنا له فلم يكن على أصلهم إضافة وجود المكون إلى التكوين أولى من إضافة وجود التكوين إلى المكون كما يشنعون علينا في مسألة الاستطاعة مع الفعل، فإما أن يترك أبو الهذيل ذلك التشنيع وينقاد للحق، وإما أن يترك هذا القول. وإلا فهو مناقض . ونقول له أيضا ، لما كان التكوين قائما بالمكون فالمكون إذا هو المكون لنفسه لما مر أن الموصوف بالصفة من قام به لا من لم يقم به، فيكون العالم على هذا خالقا لنفسه وفيه أمران أحدهما تعطيل الصانع وهو كفر، والثاني إيجاد الشيء نفسه وهو محال على ما مر في باب إثبات الصانع.
It is false, because the assertion of two pre-eternals subsisting in the Essence is impossible as previously mentioned. Likewise, making one who has attributes of perfection and is described by takwin (bringing into existence) not the maker of the world, and making one who does not have takwin the maker of it, overturns reason and is false. If that locus is originated, either it occurs by takwin or it occurs not by takwin. If it occurs not by takwin, then either it occurs without a meaning from the Creator, or it occurs by power (al-qudra). There is no way to say it occurs without a meaning from the Creator, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world and that would entail the suspension (taʿṭīl) of the Maker. And there is no way to say it occurs by power without takwin, because as previously mentioned, if this were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, so takwin would be nullified entirely. Thus the world would be something God has power over but not His creation, and God would be powerful over the world but not its Creator. Holding this is unbelief (kufr), because power (al-qudra) does not necessitate existence without the act. So this also entails the suspension of the Maker. And because if its existence were by power, then power would be bringing into existence (ījād), and bringing into existence would be eternal. If it occurs by takwin, either it occurs by a takwin prior to it, as narrated from Bishr ibn al-Muʿtamir, or it occurs by a takwin concomitant with it, as narrated from Abū l-Hudhayl. If it occurs by a takwin prior to it, then takwin cannot subsist in it before its existence, because the subsistence of an existing takwin in something not yet existing is impossible. And we have already refuted the subsistence of takwin in itself. And because if it is permissible for takwin to exist without that which is brought into existence (al-mukawwan) for one time, it is permissible for many times, since there is no difference between priority by one time and priority by many times in that its existence without that which is brought into existence is permissible. If this is so, their claim is refuted—that the existence of takwin necessarily entails the existence of the brought into existence and that priority over it is not permissible. We will explain this more fully in the question of capacity (al-istiṭāʿa), God willing. If takwin were concomitant with it, then according to their principle, attributing the existence of the brought into existence to takwin is no more appropriate than attributing the existence of takwin to the brought into existence, just as they argue against us in the question of capacity (al-istiṭāʿa) with the act. So either Abū l-Hudhayl abandons that argument and submits to the truth, or he abandons this statement. Otherwise he is contradictory. We also say to him: since takwin subsists in the brought into existence, then the brought into existence is the bringer into existence of itself, because as previously mentioned, the one described by an attribute is the one in which it subsists, not the one in which it does not subsist. Thus on this view the world would be the creator of itself, and there are two issues: first, the suspension of the Maker, which is unbelief; second, the bringing of a thing into existence by itself, which is impossible as previously mentioned in the chapter on establishing the Maker.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that takwin (bringing into existence) can have a locus (maḥall), whether that locus is pre-eternal or originated. The author (al-Nasafī) argues that takwin cannot be an attribute separate from God because it would lead to absurdities. He systematically considers two possibilities: the locus is pre-eternal or originated. If the locus is pre-eternal, that would imply two pre-eternals, which is impossible. If the locus is originated, it either occurs by takwin or not. If not by takwin, it must be by power (qudra), but this would mean the world is merely a possible thing (maqdūr) not a created thing (makhluq), leading to kufr. If by takwin, the takwin is either prior to or simultaneous with the locus. Prior takwin is impossible because takwin cannot subsist in a non-existent. Simultaneous takwin leads to a contradiction: the locus would be self-creating, which is impossible. Thus the argument concludes that takwin is not a separate attribute but identical with God's creative act.

القدرة
التعطيل

Correction: The author argues that power alone does not necessitate existence; creation requires the attribute of takwin. Otherwise, the world is merely possible, not created.

Checkpoint

A) The world becomes created in the proper sense.
B) The world is only something God has power over, not created—this is unbelief.
C) This is the correct view of the Mu'tazila.
D) It leads to two pre-eternals.

Key Takeaway
An originated locus for takwin cannot occur without takwin itself; doing so leads to either suspension of the Creator or unbelief.

In your own life, do you ever treat God's attributes as interchangeable or sufficient without understanding their distinct roles? How should this passage shape your belief about how God creates?

Originated Locus by Takwin: Prior or Concomitant
Refutes both prior and concomitant takwin as impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why takwin cannot be prior to or simultaneous with its locus, and how both options lead to absurdities including self-creation.

Core Idea
If takwin is prior to its locus, it subsists in non-existence; if concomitant, the locus creates itself.

The final part of the refutation examines the possibility that the originated locus occurs by takwin. The author considers two positions attributed to Mu'tazilī scholars: Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir (takwin prior to the locus) and Abū l-Hudhayl (takwin concomitant with the locus). He argues that both are impossible—the first because takwin cannot subsist in a non-existent thing, the second because it leads to the locus creating itself, which is both kufr and rationally impossible.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two Mu'tazilī views
Bishr says takwin precedes the locus; Abū l-Hudhayl says it is simultaneous. Both try to avoid the previous problems.
2
Refutation of prior takwin
If takwin is prior, it would be subsisting in the locus before the locus exists—impossible because an attribute cannot inhere in a non-existent.
Also, if takwin can exist without its effect for one moment, it can for many moments, undermining the claimed necessary connection.
3
Refutation of concomitant takwin
If takwin is simultaneous and subsists in the locus, then the locus is the bearer of the attribute that brings it into existence—thus it would be bringing itself into existence, which is impossible.
This results in self-creation (the world creating itself) and suspending the Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكون له باطل، إذ القول بالقديمين القائمين بالذات محال على ما مر. وكذلك جعل له من له صفات الكمال وهو موصوف بالتكوين غير صانع للعالم، وجعل من لا تكون له صانعا له قلب المعقول فيكون باطلا. وإن كان ذلك المحل حادثا إما أن حدث بتكوين وإما أن حدث لا بتكوين. فإن حدث لا بتكوين، فإما أن حدث لا بمعنى من قبل الباري، وإما أن حدث بالقدرة، ولا وجه إلى القول بحدوثه لا بمعنى من قبل الباري لأنه لو جاز ذلك فيه لجاز في جميع العالم وفيه تعطيل الصانع، ولا وجه للقول بحدوثه بالقدرة لا بتكوين لما مر أنه لو جاز هذا فيه لجاز في جميع العالم فبطل التكوين أصلا، فيكون العالم مقدور الله تعالى لا مخلوقه، ويكون الله قادرا على العالم لا خالقا له، والقول به كفر لما أن القدرة لا تقتضى الوجود بدون الفعل، فيكون فيه أيضا تعطيل الصانع. ولأن وجوده لو كان بالقدرة لكانت القدرة إيجادا وهي فكان الإيجاد أزليا. ولو حدث بتكوين إما أن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه كما هو المحكي عن بشر بن المعتمر، وإما أن حدث بتكوين مقارن له كما هو المحكي عن أبي الهذيل، فإن حدث بتكوين سابق عليه فإذا لا قيام للتكوين به قبل وجوده إذ قيام تكوين موجود بمكون لم يوجد بعد محال، وقد أبطلنا قيام التكوين بنفسه، ولأنه لما جاز وجود التكوين ولا مكون بعد زمانا واحدا جاز أزمنة كثيرة إذ لا فرق بين التقدم بزمان والتقدم بأزمنة في أن وجوده ولا مكون جائز . وإذا كان كذلك بطل ادعاؤهم – أن وجود التكوين يقتضي وجود المكون لا محالة ولا يجوز سبقه عليه ـ ونبين هذا بأتم من ذلك في مسألة الاستطاعة – إن شاء الله تعالى. ولو كان التكوين مقارنا له فلم يكن على أصلهم إضافة وجود المكون إلى التكوين أولى من إضافة وجود التكوين إلى المكون كما يشنعون علينا في مسألة الاستطاعة مع الفعل، فإما أن يترك أبو الهذيل ذلك التشنيع وينقاد للحق، وإما أن يترك هذا القول. وإلا فهو مناقض . ونقول له أيضا ، لما كان التكوين قائما بالمكون فالمكون إذا هو المكون لنفسه لما مر أن الموصوف بالصفة من قام به لا من لم يقم به، فيكون العالم على هذا خالقا لنفسه وفيه أمران أحدهما تعطيل الصانع وهو كفر، والثاني إيجاد الشيء نفسه وهو محال على ما مر في باب إثبات الصانع.
It is false, because the assertion of two pre-eternals subsisting in the Essence is impossible as previously mentioned. Likewise, making one who has attributes of perfection and is described by takwin (bringing into existence) not the maker of the world, and making one who does not have takwin the maker of it, overturns reason and is false. If that locus is originated, either it occurs by takwin or it occurs not by takwin. If it occurs not by takwin, then either it occurs without a meaning from the Creator, or it occurs by power (al-qudra). There is no way to say it occurs without a meaning from the Creator, because if that were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world and that would entail the suspension (taʿṭīl) of the Maker. And there is no way to say it occurs by power without takwin, because as previously mentioned, if this were permissible for it, it would be permissible for the entire world, so takwin would be nullified entirely. Thus the world would be something God has power over but not His creation, and God would be powerful over the world but not its Creator. Holding this is unbelief (kufr), because power (al-qudra) does not necessitate existence without the act. So this also entails the suspension of the Maker. And because if its existence were by power, then power would be bringing into existence (ījād), and bringing into existence would be eternal. If it occurs by takwin, either it occurs by a takwin prior to it, as narrated from Bishr ibn al-Muʿtamir, or it occurs by a takwin concomitant with it, as narrated from Abū l-Hudhayl. If it occurs by a takwin prior to it, then takwin cannot subsist in it before its existence, because the subsistence of an existing takwin in something not yet existing is impossible. And we have already refuted the subsistence of takwin in itself. And because if it is permissible for takwin to exist without that which is brought into existence (al-mukawwan) for one time, it is permissible for many times, since there is no difference between priority by one time and priority by many times in that its existence without that which is brought into existence is permissible. If this is so, their claim is refuted—that the existence of takwin necessarily entails the existence of the brought into existence and that priority over it is not permissible. We will explain this more fully in the question of capacity (al-istiṭāʿa), God willing. If takwin were concomitant with it, then according to their principle, attributing the existence of the brought into existence to takwin is no more appropriate than attributing the existence of takwin to the brought into existence, just as they argue against us in the question of capacity (al-istiṭāʿa) with the act. So either Abū l-Hudhayl abandons that argument and submits to the truth, or he abandons this statement. Otherwise he is contradictory. We also say to him: since takwin subsists in the brought into existence, then the brought into existence is the bringer into existence of itself, because as previously mentioned, the one described by an attribute is the one in which it subsists, not the one in which it does not subsist. Thus on this view the world would be the creator of itself, and there are two issues: first, the suspension of the Maker, which is unbelief; second, the bringing of a thing into existence by itself, which is impossible as previously mentioned in the chapter on establishing the Maker.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that takwin (bringing into existence) can have a locus (maḥall), whether that locus is pre-eternal or originated. The author (al-Nasafī) argues that takwin cannot be an attribute separate from God because it would lead to absurdities. He systematically considers two possibilities: the locus is pre-eternal or originated. If the locus is pre-eternal, that would imply two pre-eternals, which is impossible. If by takwin, the takwin is either prior to or simultaneous with the locus. Prior takwin is impossible because takwin cannot subsist in a non-existent. Simultaneous takwin leads to a contradiction: the locus would be self-creating, which is impossible. Thus the argument concludes that takwin is not a separate attribute but identical with God's creative act.

The Karramiyyah Doctrine of Originated Takwin in God
Describes and refutes the Karramiyyah doctrine of originated events in God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Karramiyyah claim that originated events (takwin, will, speech) occur in God's Essence and why this is declared impossible.

Core Idea
The Karramiyyah make God a locus of temporal events, contradicting divine transcendence.

The author begins by declaring the Karramiyyah view impossible, then explains the need to state their doctrine so its falsehood becomes clear. He then presents their belief that takwin, will, and speech are originated in God's Essence, involving multiple temporal events for each act of creation or annihilation. This lesson presents their doctrine and the initial critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the author's argument. Notice the strong opening declaration and the structured presentation of the Karramiyyah view.
The passage ends mid-sentence due to a page break; focus on the presented content.
2
Identify the Karramiyyah view
Identify what the Karramiyyah claim about takwin, will, and speech in God's Essence. Note that they say each act of bringing into existence or annihilation involves multiple originated events in God.
3
Understand the implication
Reflect on why the author calls this impossible. The key problem is that it makes God's essence a locus for temporal events (ḥawādith), which is incompatible with divine immutability and perfection.
This connects to the broader Aqeedah principle that God is not subject to change or temporal origination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حدوث التكوين في ذات الباري كما يذهب إليه الكرامية فمحال. ولابد من بيان مذهبهم في هذا ليظهر عند الوقوف على فحض جهالتهم، بطلان مقالتهم قبل الاشتغال بإبطال مذهبهم وإدحاض شبهتهم. [كلام للكرامية]. فنقول : إن مذهبهم إن كان ما يريد الله إحداثه في العالم يحدث في ذاته إحداثه وتكوينه ويحدث إرادة حدوثه فيريد بإرادات حادثة ويتكلم بكلام حادث في ذاته من جنس الحروف فيحدث بقوله "كن" كان، وقول "وترزق": ترزق حادث. ويزعمون أن الحوادث التي تحدث في ذات الله تعالى أضعاف المحدثات من الأجسام والأعراض إذ لا حدوث لشيء من أجزاء العالم إلا بقوله: "كن" وإرادته لحدوثه، وهما حادثان في ذاته، ولا ينعدم شيء من أجزاء العالم إلا بقوله "افْنَ" أو كن معدوما، وإرادته لعدمه وهما حادثان في ذاته، فكانت الحوادث في ذاته أضعاف
As for the origination of takwin (bringing into existence) in the Essence of the Creator, as the Karramiyyah hold, it is impossible. It is necessary to state their doctrine on this so that when one stands upon the extent of their ignorance, the falsehood of their statement becomes manifest before engaging in refuting their doctrine and disproving their doubts. [Speech of the Karramiyyah.] We say: Their doctrine is that what God wills to bring into originated existence in the world occurs in His Essence: its bringing into existence (ījād) and its takwin, and He originates the will for its origination, so He wills by originated wills, and He speaks by an originated speech in His Essence of the kind of letters, so by His saying "Be" it becomes, and His saying "and you provide" means you provide is originated. And they claim that the originated events (ḥawādith) that occur in the Essence of God Most High are many times more than the originated things of bodies and accidents, since nothing of the parts of the world comes into existence except by His saying "Be" and His will for its origination, and both are originated in His Essence; and nothing of the parts of the world becomes nonexistent except by His saying "Perish" or "Be nonexistent" and His will for its nonexistence, and both are originated in His Essence. So the originated events in His Essence are many times more...
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Karramiyyah sect's doctrine that takwin (bringing into existence) and other events originate in God's Essence. The author first declares this view impossible, then explains that it is necessary to describe their doctrine so that its falsehood is clear. He then presents their view: they believe that when God wants to bring something into existence, the act of bringing into existence (ījād) and takwin occur in God's Essence, along with an originated will. Similarly, God speaks with an originated speech consisting of letters, so His command 'Be' is an originated event in His Essence. They claim that the number of originated events in God's Essence exceeds the number of all originated things in the world, because every coming-to-be and passing-away involves multiple originated events in God. The author will later refute this, but here he only presents the doctrine to show its absurdity: it makes God a locus for temporal events (ḥawādith), which is incompatible with divine transcendence.

Refutation of Abu al-Hudhayl on Takwin
Nasafi refutes Abu al-Hudhayl's claim that takwin is concomitant with the thing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Abu al-Hudhayl's claim that takwin is concomitant with the thing leads to logical inconsistency and theological absurdity.

Core Idea
Takwin cannot be concomitant with the thing without causing self-creation or denial of God.

Abu al-Hudhayl argued that takwin (God's act of bringing into existence) is simultaneous with the thing brought into existence. But this seemingly simple claim has grave consequences. In this lesson, Nasafi exposes two fatal problems with this view: it undermines the very logic Abu al-Hudhayl uses elsewhere, and it implies that the world creates itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how Nasafi presents two distinct arguments.
2
Understand the first argument: inconsistency with istita'a
The passage shows that if takwin is concomitant with the thing, then there is no reason to prefer attributing existence to one over the other—the same logic Abu al-Hudhayl uses against others in the issue of istita'a. Thus he is contradictory unless he abandons one position.
This argument is based on symmetry.
3
Understand the second argument: subsistence leads to self-creation
Nasafi argues that if takwin subsists in the thing, then the thing would be its own bringer into existence, because an attribute belongs to the one in which it subsists. This leads to the world being its own creator, which is kufr and impossible.
This argument is based on the principle of subsistence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان التكوين مقارنا له فلم يكن على أصلهم إضافة وجود المكون إلى التكوين أولى من إضافة وجود التكوين إلى المكون كما يشنعون علينا في مسألة الاستطاعة مع الفعل، فإما أن يترك أبو الهذيل ذلك التشنيع وينقاد للحق، وإما أن يترك هذا القول. وإلا فهو مناقض . ونقول له أيضا ، لما كان التكوين قائما بالمكون فالمكون إذا هو المكون لنفسه لما مر أن الموصوف بالصفة من قام به لا من لم يقم به، فيكون العالم على هذا خالقا لنفسه وفيه أمران أحدهما تعطيل الصانع وهو كفر، والثاني إيجاد الشيء نفسه وهو محال على ما مر في باب إثبات الصانع.
If takwin (bringing into existence) were concomitant with the thing (al-mukawwan), then according to their principle it would not be more preferable to attribute the existence of the thing to takwin than to attribute the existence of takwin to the thing—just as they reproach us in the issue of istita'a (power/ability) with the act. So either Abu al-Hudhayl abandons that reproach and submits to the truth, or he abandons this statement. Otherwise he is contradictory. And we also say to him: Since takwin subsists in the thing (al-mukawwan), then the thing is its own bringer into existence (mukawwin li-nafsihi), because—as has preceded—the one described by an attribute is the one in which it subsists, not the one in which it does not subsist. Thus on this basis the world would be its own creator. In this are two matters: one is denial of the Maker (ta'til al-sani'), which is unbelief; the second is a thing bringing itself into existence, which is impossible, as has preceded in the chapter on establishing the Maker.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Abu al-Hudhayl's position on the relationship between takwin (God's act of bringing into existence) and the thing brought into existence (mukawwan). The author argues that if takwin is concomitant with the thing (i.e., not distinct or prior), then there is no reason to attribute the existence of the thing to takwin rather than the existence of takwin to the thing—a point Abu al-Hudhayl himself uses against others in the issue of istita'a and the act. Thus Abu al-Hudhayl is inconsistent unless he abandons his reproach or his own statement. Furthermore, if takwin subsists in the thing, then the thing would be its own bringer into existence, since an attribute belongs to the one in which it subsists. This leads to absurdity: the world would be its own creator, implying either denial of God (kufr) or self-creation, both impossible.

Key Terms
تكوين
مكون
استطاعة
تعطيل الصانع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think takwin is an inherent property of the thing, so it is concomitant.
Correction: The author shows this leads to the absurdity that the thing would be its own creator, implying denial of God or self-creation, both impossible.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, if takwin is concomitant with the thing, what absurd consequence follows?
A) The thing would be eternal.
B) The thing would be its own creator.
C) The thing would be nonexistent.
D) Takwin would be unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes Abu al-Hudhayl by showing that if takwin is concomitant with the thing, it leads to logical inconsistency and the blasphemous conclusion that the world creates itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own existence, do you recognize that it is entirely dependent on God's act of creation? How does this passage's refutation of self-creation challenge any subtle feeling of self-sufficiency you might harbor? What step will you take today to consciously affirm your absolute need for God?
?
This passage warns against attributing creation to anything other than God. Are there areas in your life where you unconsciously attribute power or causation to created things—like your own efforts, money, or people—as if they are independent creators? What specific thought or action will you change to redirect all causality to God?
?
Nasafi's argument forces us to consider the logical consequences of our beliefs. In what ways do you hold contradictory positions about God's attributes? How can you seek a more consistent understanding of tawhid, even if it requires abandoning comfortable but flawed ideas?

The Impossibility of Temporal Takwin in God's Essence
Nasafi declares the Karramiyya view impossible and states the need to expose their doctrine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's firm declaration that the occurrence of takwin (bringing into existence) in Allah's essence is impossible, and why it is necessary to expose the Karramiyya doctrine before refuting it.

Core Idea
Temporal events cannot occur in God's essence—this is impossible.

Before delving into the details of the Karramiyya position, Nasafi sets the tone by declaring their central claim impossible. He then explains why we must first understand their doctrine thoroughly before attempting to refute it. This lesson establishes the starting point of the discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the short Arabic passage carefully. Note the decisive tone of the word 'muhal' (impossible).
2
Understand the necessity of explanation
Nasafi says it is necessary to explain the Karramiyya doctrine so that their ignorance becomes apparent. Ask: Why is it important to understand a false view before refuting it?
3
Connect to the larger discussion
Realize that this lesson sets the foundation for the detailed exposition of the Karramiyya in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حدوث التكوين في ذات الباري كما يذهب إليه الكرامية فمحال. ولابد من بيان مذهبهم في هذا ليظهر عند الوقوف على فحض جهالتهم، بطلان مقالتهم قبل الاشتغال بإبطال مذهبهم وإدحاض شبهتهم. فنقول : إن مذهبهم إن كان ما يريد الله إحداثه في العالم يحدث في ذاته إحداثه وتكوينه ويحدث إرادة حدوثه فيريد بإرادات حادثة ويتكلم بكلام حادث في ذاته من جنس الحروف فيحدث بقوله "كن" كان، وقول "وترزق": ترزق حادث. ويزعمون أن الحوادث التي تحدث في ذات الله تعالى أضعاف المحدثات من الأجسام والأعراض إذ لا حدوث لشيء من أجزاء العالم إلا بقوله: "كن" وإرادته لحدوثه، وهما حادثان في ذاته، ولا ينعدم شيء من أجزاء العالم إلا بقوله "افْنَ" أو كن معدوما، وإرادته لعدمه وهما حادثان في ذاته، فكانت الحوادث في ذاته أضعاف محدثات العالم. وكذا قالوا بحدوث مماسة في ذاته عند مماسته لما يماس من الأجسام، وكذا عند رؤيته شيئا أو سماعه صوتا يحدث فيه تسمع وتبصر المبصرات والمرئيات ويسمونه سميعا في الأزل لا بسمع قائم بذاته بل بسمعيته يعددون به قدرته على السمع، وكذا يسمونه بصيرا ببصريته، ثم تبصره وتسمعه محدثان، وكذا كان في الأزل متكلما قائلا لا بقوله وكلامه بل بقائليته ومتكلميته، وهما قدرته على القول والكلام، فأما الكلام فهو يحدث عند تكلمه. وكذا كان في الأزل خالقا بخالقيته ورازقا برازقيته، وهما القدرة على الرزق وعلى الخلق، فأما الخلق والرزق فهما يحدثان في ذاته. هذا هو مذهب جمهورهم
As for the occurrence (huduth) of takwin in the essence of the Almighty—as the Karramiyya hold—it is impossible. It is necessary to explain their doctrine in this so that when one stops at the depth of their ignorance, the falsity of their statement becomes apparent before engaging in refuting their doctrine and rebutting their doubts. So we say: Their doctrine is that whatever God intends to bring about in the world occurs in His essence—its bringing about and its takwin—and He brings about the will for its occurrence, so He wills with temporal wills, and He speaks with temporal speech in His essence of the genus of letters. So He brings about by His saying 'Kun' (Be) it is, and His saying 'And You provide' (wa tarzuq) has a temporal providing. And they claim that the temporal events that occur in God's essence are manyfold more than the created things of bodies and accidents, since no thing from among the parts of the world occurs except by His saying 'Kun' and His will for its occurrence, and these two are temporal in His essence; and no thing from among the parts of the world ceases to exist except by His saying 'Ifna' (Perish) or 'Be nonexistent' and His will for its nonexistence, and these two are temporal in His essence. So the temporal events in His essence are manyfold more than the created things of the world. Likewise, they said that there is a temporal occurrence of touching (mumassa) in His essence when He touches what He touches of bodies; likewise, when He sees something or hears a sound, there occurs in Him a hearing and seeing of the seen and heard things, and they name Him 'Hearing' (Sami') in pre-eternity not by a hearing subsisting in His essence but by His 'hearingness' (sam'iyya), by which they enumerate His power over hearing; likewise they name Him 'Seeing' (Basir) by His 'seeingness' (basariyya); then His seeing and hearing are temporal. Likewise, He was in pre-eternity a Speaker (mutakallim), a Sayer (qa'il) not by His saying (qawl) and speech (kalam) but by His 'sayerness' (qa'iliyya) and 'speakerhood' (mutakallimiyya), and these two are His power over saying and speech; as for speech, it occurs when He speaks. Likewise, He was in pre-eternity a Creator (khaliq) by His 'creatorship' (khaliqiyya) and a Provider (raziq) by His 'providership' (raziqiyya), and these two are the power over providing and creating; as for creation (khalq) and provision (rizq), they occur in His essence. This is the doctrine of the majority of them.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage begins by declaring that the Karramiyya view of temporal events occurring in God's essence is impossible. The author then states the necessity of explaining their doctrine to reveal their ignorance before engaging in formal refutation. The exposition details that according to the Karramiyya, whenever God intends to create something, He first creates the act of bringing it into existence (takwin) and the will for it within His own essence. Similarly, His speech ('Kun') and will are temporal events in His essence. They claim that these temporal events in God are far more numerous than the created things themselves, because each thing requires both a creative command and a will. They also hold that physical touching, seeing, and hearing involve temporal events of touching, hearing, and seeing in God's essence, though God is eternally described as Hearing and Seeing by powers (sam'iyya, basariyya) rather than by subsisting attributes. Similarly, God is eternally a Speaker by a power (qa'iliyya) but speech itself occurs temporally when He speaks. The same applies to creation and provision: God is eternally a Creator and Provider by powers (khaliqiyya, raziqiyya), but the acts of creating and providing are temporal events in His essence. This is stated as the view of their majority.

Key Terms
تكوين
كرامية
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that God's act of creation involves temporal changes in His essence.
Correction: Nasafi declares that any temporal occurrence in God's essence is impossible, regardless of whether it is called takwin or anything else.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi say about the occurrence of takwin in God's essence, according to the passage?
A) It is possible only through will.
B) It is impossible.
C) It is necessary.
D) It is a matter of debate.

Key Takeaway
The occurrence of any temporal event in God's essence is categorically impossible, and exposing the Karramiyya's doctrine requires careful exposition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage insists that temporal events cannot occur in God's essence. Have you ever allowed your own sense of God as 'active' to subtly imply that He undergoes change? How will you guard your heart against such a thought?
?
Nasafi says that by explaining the Karramiyya doctrine, the depth of their ignorance becomes apparent before formal refutation. When you encounter a belief you know is false, are you quick to dismiss it without first understanding it? Commit to one relationship where you will listen carefully before correcting.

Divine Attributes
advanced
8 min
The Karramiyya Doctrine of Temporal Events in God's Essence
Nasafi exposits the Karramiyya doctrine of temporal events in God's essence in detail.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed claims of the Karramiyya regarding temporal events in God's essence, including takwin, will, speech, touching, seeing, hearing, creation, and provision.

Core Idea
The Karramiyya believe countless temporal events occur in God's essence for each act of creation and annihilation.

Having declared the Karramiyya view impossible, Nasafi now exposits their doctrine in full. He details how they envision temporal events such as commands, wills, and even physical touch occurring in God's essence. This lesson carefully unpacks each claim to reveal the inner logic of their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
This is a long passage. Read it once to get the gist, then read the translation. Notice the repetitive structure: for each type of attribute, they posit a power (like sam'iyya) and a temporal event.
The passage is dense but systematic.
2
Identify the core claim about multiplication
The Karramiyya argue that temporal events in God are manyfold more than created things because each created thing requires a command and a will. Count the examples: existence commands, annihilation commands, touching, seeing, hearing, speech, creation, provision.
3
Understand their view on divine attributes
Note that they say God is eternally Hearing, Seeing, etc. by powers (sam'iyya, basariyya), but the actual acts of hearing, seeing are temporal events in His essence. Compare this with the orthodox view that God's attributes are eternal.
4
Reflect on the overall picture
Consider why Nasafi calls this 'the depth of their ignorance'. Think about how positing temporal events in God compromises His immutability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حدوث التكوين في ذات الباري كما يذهب إليه الكرامية فمحال. ولابد من بيان مذهبهم في هذا ليظهر عند الوقوف على فحض جهالتهم، بطلان مقالتهم قبل الاشتغال بإبطال مذهبهم وإدحاض شبهتهم. فنقول : إن مذهبهم إن كان ما يريد الله إحداثه في العالم يحدث في ذاته إحداثه وتكوينه ويحدث إرادة حدوثه فيريد بإرادات حادثة ويتكلم بكلام حادث في ذاته من جنس الحروف فيحدث بقوله "كن" كان، وقول "وترزق": ترزق حادث. ويزعمون أن الحوادث التي تحدث في ذات الله تعالى أضعاف المحدثات من الأجسام والأعراض إذ لا حدوث لشيء من أجزاء العالم إلا بقوله: "كن" وإرادته لحدوثه، وهما حادثان في ذاته، ولا ينعدم شيء من أجزاء العالم إلا بقوله "افْنَ" أو كن معدوما، وإرادته لعدمه وهما حادثان في ذاته، فكانت الحوادث في ذاته أضعاف محدثات العالم. وكذا قالوا بحدوث مماسة في ذاته عند مماسته لما يماس من الأجسام، وكذا عند رؤيته شيئا أو سماعه صوتا يحدث فيه تسمع وتبصر المبصرات والمرئيات ويسمونه سميعا في الأزل لا بسمع قائم بذاته بل بسمعيته يعددون به قدرته على السمع، وكذا يسمونه بصيرا ببصريته، ثم تبصره وتسمعه محدثان، وكذا كان في الأزل متكلما قائلا لا بقوله وكلامه بل بقائليته ومتكلميته، وهما قدرته على القول والكلام، فأما الكلام فهو يحدث عند تكلمه. وكذا كان في الأزل خالقا بخالقيته ورازقا برازقيته، وهما القدرة على الرزق وعلى الخلق، فأما الخلق والرزق فهما يحدثان في ذاته. هذا هو مذهب جمهورهم

So He brings about by His saying 'Kun' (Be) it is, and His saying 'And You provide' (wa tarzuq) has a temporal providing. And they claim that the temporal events that occur in God's essence are manyfold more than the created things of bodies and accidents, since no thing from among the parts of the world occurs except by His saying 'Kun' and His will for its occurrence, and these two are temporal in His essence; and no thing from among the parts of the world ceases to exist except by His saying 'Ifna' (Perish) or 'Be nonexistent' and His will for its nonexistence, and these two are temporal in His essence. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's attributes like hearing, seeing, speech, creation, and provision are eternal acts subsisting in His essence.
Correction: The Karramiyya wrongly posit that these acts are temporal events occurring in God's essence, while the orthodox view holds that God's attributes are eternal and not subject to temporal change.

Checkpoint
According to the Karramiyya doctrine as described in this passage, what is true about the number of temporal events in God's essence compared to created things?
A) They are equal in number.
B) They are fewer.
C) They are manyfold more.
D) There are no temporal events in God's essence.

Key Takeaway
The Karramiyya doctrine posits a vast number of temporal events in God's essence for every act of creation and annihilation, including commands, wills, touching, seeing, hearing, speech, creation, and provision.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Karramiyya say that God's seeing and hearing are temporal events that occur in His essence. If you truly believed that every moment you are being 'seen' and 'heard' in a real, temporal way by the Creator, what would you change about how you live today?
?
Consider that the Karramiyya claim for every created thing there are two temporal events in God's essence. Does this sense of God's constant involvement in every detail of creation inspire awe in you, or does it reveal how seldom you acknowledge His presence in your daily decisions? What one action can you take today to make His presence more real to you?
?
The Karramiyya distinguish between God's pre-eternal powers (like sayerness) and His temporal speech. How often do you think about the gap between what you have the power to say and what you actually say? Will you commit to speaking only words that could be worthy of being 'temporal events' in the sight of God?
